2:28:1661:0:14:72:331:700:12:Times:12:Times:The Monopoly of Violence: Evidence from Colombia
2:29:1709:14:14:72:347:686:12:Times:12:Times:Daron Acemoglu, James A. Robinson, and Rafael Santos
2:30:1761:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 15578
2:31:1789:14:14:72:148:658:12:Times:12:Times:December 2009
2:32:1802:14:28:72:153:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. D7,H11
2:33:1816:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:34:1824:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:Many states in Latin America, Africa and Asia lack the monopoly of violence, identified by Max Weber
2:35:1924:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:as the foundation of the state, and thus the capacity to govern effectively. In this paper we develop
2:36:2025:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:a new perspective on the establishment of the monopoly of violence and the formation of the state.
2:37:2123:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:We build a model to explain the incentive of central states to eliminate non-state armed actors (paramilitaries)
2:38:2235:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:in a democracy. The model is premised on the idea that paramilitaries may choose to and can influence
2:39:2336:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:elections. Since paramilitaries have preferences over policies, this reduces the incentives of the politicians
2:40:2446:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:they favor to eliminate them. The model also shows that while in non-paramilitary areas policies are
2:41:2546:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:targeted at citizens, in paramilitary controlled areas they are targeted at paramilitaries. We then investigate
2:42:2657:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:the predictions of our model using data from Colombia between 1991 and 2006. We first present regression
2:43:2761:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:and case study evidence supporting our postulate that paramilitary groups can have significant effects
2:44:2863:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:on elections for the legislature and the executive. Next, we show that the evidence is also broadly consistent
2:45:2973:14:14:72:540:434:12:Times:12:Times:with the implication of the model that paramilitaries tend to persist to the extent that they deliver votes
2:46:3080:14:14:72:540:420:12:Times:12:Times:to candidates for the executive whose preferences are close to theirs and that this effect is larger in
2:47:3183:14:14:72:540:406:12:Times:12:Times:areas where the Presidential candidate would have otherwise not done as well. These results illustrate
2:48:3285:14:14:72:540:392:12:Times:12:Times:that, consistent with our model, there appears to be a symbiotic relationship between some executives
2:49:3386:14:14:72:540:378:12:Times:12:Times:and paramilitaries. Finally, we use roll-call votes to illustrate a possible ‘quid pro quo’ between the
2:50:3489:14:42:72:273:364:12:Times:12:Times:executive and paramilitaries in Colombia.
2:51:3530:42:14:72:155:322:12:Times:12:Times:Daron Acemoglu
2:52:3544:14:14:72:198:308:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:53:3567:14:14:72:149:294:12:Times:12:Times:MIT, E52-380B
2:54:3580:14:14:72:165:280:12:Times:12:Times:50 Memorial Drive

2:58:3650:28:14:72:165:210:12:Times:12:Times:James A. Robinson
2:59:3667:14:14:72:165:196:12:Times:12:Times:Harvard University

2:61:3709:14:14:72:216:168:12:Times:12:Times:N309, 1737 Cambridge Street

2:63:3756:14:14:72:165:140:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER, CIFAR
2:64:3771:14:0:72:206:126:12:Times:12:Times:jrobinson@gov.harvard.edu
2:65:3796:0:14:306:372:322:12:Times:12:Times:Rafael Santos
2:66:3809:14:14:306:382:308:12:Times:12:Times:Yale University

3:68:3855:0:35:126:440:679:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\Political power grows out of the barrel of a gun."|Mao Zedong.
3:69:3918:35:27:82:195:644:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:1  Introduction
3:70:3933:27:17:82:543:617:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Many scholars have argued that di-erences in state capacity are a key factor in comparative
3:71:4024:17:17:82:543:600:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:economic and political development (see for instance Evans, Rueschemeyer and Skocpol, 1985,
3:72:4115:17:17:82:543:583:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Evans, 1989, 1995, Kohli, 2004).  Although state capacity is multi-faceted, it inevitably relies
3:73:4211:17:17:82:543:566:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on Weber's famous notion of the state as \a human community that (successfully) claims the
3:74:4301:17:18:82:543:549:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f2:monopoly of the legitimate use of physical forcewithin a given territory" (1946, p. 78). States
3:75:4396:18:17:82:543:531:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:vary greatly in their capacities and whether or not they have such a monopoly of violence, and
3:76:4490:17:17:82:543:514:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:there is little evidence that this variation has decreased over the recent past. For example, in the
3:77:4590:17:17:82:543:497:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1990s the state in Somalia, Sierra Leone, Liberia, the Congo and Rwanda, completely collapsed
3:78:4683:17:17:82:543:480:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and gave up any pretence of undertaking the tasks that we associate with states. In Latin America,
3:79:4781:17:17:82:543:463:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Colombia, Peru, Guatemala, El Salvador, and Nicaragua have all recently experienced or are now
3:80:4875:17:17:82:543:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:experiencing prolonged civil wars, with the writ of the state being absent from large parts of the
3:81:4973:17:17:82:543:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:country. In Pakistan the central state in Islamabad has little control of the `tribal areas' such as
3:82:5073:17:17:82:502:412:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Waziristan. Similarly, the Iraqi state in Baghdad exercises little authority in Kurdistan.
3:83:5163:17:17:99:543:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Why do some states fail to establish this monopoly? The social science literature emphasizes
3:84:5255:17:17:82:543:378:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:several key ideas, for instance, the inability of states to establish such monopoly because of
3:85:5349:17:17:82:543:361:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:`di-cult geography' (Herbst, 2000), `rough terrain' (Fearon and Laitin, 2003), or simply poverty
3:86:5445:17:17:82:543:344:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(Fearon and Laitin, 2003). It has also suggested that inter-state competition and warfare (Hintze,
3:87:5543:17:17:82:543:327:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1975, Tilly, 1975, 1990, Brewer, 1988, Herbst, 2000, Bates, 2001, Centeno, 2002) and domestic
3:88:5636:17:17:82:543:310:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:political competition in\ruence the incentives of politicians to build state capacity (Acemoglu,
3:89:5732:17:17:82:543:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Ticchi, Vindigni, 2006, Besley and Persson, 2007). Common to all of these explanations is a type
3:90:5828:17:17:82:543:276:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of `modernization' view, suggesting that as society modernizes and grows richer, state capacity
3:91:5923:17:17:82:543:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:will simultaneously develop.  In particular `state formation' involves eliminating armed actors
3:92:6018:17:17:82:543:242:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and establishing a monopoly of violence, in the same way that after the Wars of the Roses the
3:93:6111:17:17:82:399:225:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:victorious Tudors disarmed the English aristocracy (Storey, 1968).
3:94:6177:17:17:99:543:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Yet several of the examples above are quite puzzling from this point of view. In the case of
3:95:6269:17:17:82:543:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Pakistan, the tribal areas have existed since the formation of the country in 1947, and even though
3:96:6368:17:17:82:543:174:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:they have been largely out of the control of the central state, they have also been represented
3:97:6463:17:17:82:543:157:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:within it. Under the 1973 Constitution the tribal areas had 8 representatives in the National
3:98:6556:17:17:82:543:140:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Assembly elected by the tribal elders, or the Maliks. Under General Musharraf's regime this was
3:99:6651:17:17:82:543:123:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:increased to 12. In Iraq, while the peshmerga militia control the streets of Mosul, a coalition of
3:100:6749:17:17:82:543:106:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Kurdish political parties keeps the government in power in Baghdad. In Colombia, as we shall
3:101:6841:17:0:82:543:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:see, as much as one third of the legislature may have been elected in elections heavily in\ruenced
4:102:6940:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by armed paramilitary groups. After many of these were arrested by the Supreme Court, the
4:103:7029:17:17:82:481:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Colombian President did little to stop their alternates from voting in their absence.
4:104:7114:17:17:99:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:These examples point to a di-erent path of state formation than the one taken by England
4:105:7202:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:under the Tudors and subsequently enshrined in the social science literature. Instead, they sug-
4:106:7298:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:gest that state formation can take place without a monopoly of violence being established. In this
4:107:7396:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paper we develop a new perspective on state formation, emphasizing the idea that aspects of state
4:108:7493:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:weakness, particularly the lack of monopoly of violence in peripheral areas, can be an equilibrium
4:109:7591:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:outcome. Moreover, in contrast to the implicit notion common in the previous literature, `mod-
4:110:7685:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ernization' need not automatically eradicate non-state armed actors. Although we believe that
4:111:7778:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the ideas proposed in this paper have relevance both in democratic or non-democratic contexts,
4:112:7872:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we develop a model formalizing these notions in the context of a democratic country. We then
4:113:7964:17:17:82:439:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:investigate several of implications of this model using data from Colombia.
4:114:8039:17:17:99:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our model begins from the observation that in a democracy non-state armed actors (in our
4:115:8127:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:context, paramilitaries) can control citizens' voting behavior. Since paramilitaries naturally have
4:116:8226:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:preferences over policies, when they choose to become involved in politics, this reduces the incen-
4:117:8325:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tives of the politicians they favor to eliminate them. The model predicts that in non-paramilitary
4:118:8423:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:areas policies are targeted at citizens while in paramilitary areas they cater to the preferences of
4:119:8523:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries. This implies that in paramilitary areas citizens obtain fewer public goods (and
4:120:8618:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:other policies they value). The model further implies that paramilitaries will tend to persist to
4:121:8715:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the extent that they deliver votes to politicians they prefer|in the Colombian case, to Presi-
4:122:8809:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dent-Alvaro Uribe|and that this e-ect is stronger in areas where these politicians would have
4:123:8902:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:otherwise not done as well.  Thus non-state armed actors can persist because they can be in
4:124:8993:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a symbiotic relationship with speci\fc politicians holding power: paramilitaries deliver votes to
4:125:9090:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:politicians with preferences relatively close to theirs, while politicians they helped elect implicitly
4:126:9193:17:17:82:346:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:or explicitly support laws and policies that they prefer.
4:127:9250:17:17:99:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We empirically investigate the implications of our model using the recent Colombian experi-
4:128:9341:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ence, where two main non-state armed actors, the `left-wing' guerrillas Fuerzas Armadas Revolu-
4:129:9436:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:cionarias de Colombia (FARC|The Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia) and `right-wing'
4:130:9524:17:17:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary forces, which in 1997 coalesced into the Autodefensas Unidas de Colombia (AUC|
4:131:9615:17:17:82:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:United Self-Defense Organization of Colombia), have shaped the recent political landscape. We
4:132:9708:17:17:82:543:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\frst provide evidence that paramilitaries, though interestingly not the FARC, have systematically
4:133:9806:17:17:82:543:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in\ruenced electoral outcomes. In particular, after the AUC got involved in politics in 2001, the
4:134:9903:17:17:82:543:163:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence of paramilitaries in a municipality is correlated with the rise of non-traditional `third
4:135:10001:17:17:82:543:146:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:parties' (that is, parties other than the Liberals, the Conservatives, and the Socialists), which are
4:136:10102:17:17:82:543:129:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:widely recognized to be often directly or indirectly associated with the paramilitaries (e.g., L-opez,
4:137:10204:17:17:82:543:112:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2007, Valencia, 2007). We also \fnd that paramilitary presence is also associated with a greater
4:138:10300:17:0:82:543:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:concentration of votes within a municipality in legislative elections and with greater support for
5:139:10399:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:President-Alvaro Uribe, who has enacted several key policies in line with the preferences of the
5:140:10495:17:17:82:288:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries, in the presidential elections.
5:141:10541:17:17:99:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The e-ect of paramilitaries on the elections is further substantiated by the fact that when a
5:142:10634:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:senator's list receives a greater proportion of its votes in areas with high paramilitary presence,
5:143:10733:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the senator is more likely to be subsequently arrested for illegal connections with paramilitaries
5:144:10831:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and to support the two clauses of the Justice and Peace Law that were highly lenient towards
5:145:10923:17:17:82:544:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the paramilitaries.1Table 1 depicts some of the relevant information. On it we placed the 20
5:146:11015:17:17:82:542:589:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:senators whose list got the greatest share of their votes in areas with high paramilitary presence.2
5:147:11115:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Column 1 shows that 45% of these senators belong to `third political parties'. Column 4 shows
5:148:11208:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that the two senators with the highest vote shares have been arrested and found guilty of links
5:149:11303:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with paramilitary groups. As of May 2009 another 4 senators are under arrest, while a further
5:150:11396:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:3 are under investigation, all for links with paramilitaries. Column 3 shows that the majority of
5:151:11493:17:17:82:479:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:those in o-ce at the time also supported the clauses of the Justice and Peace Law.
5:152:11575:17:17:99:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The evidence mentioned so far is consistent with the assumptions of our model, that paramil-
5:153:11667:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:itaries were actively involved in in\ruencing elections. The main prediction of our model is that
5:154:11764:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries should persist more where they deliver votes to the executive that they prefer,
5:155:11858:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:particularly in areas where this politician would otherwise not do well. This is because elimi-
5:156:11953:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:nating paramilitaries would implicitly cost valuable votes in the election. We also show that the
5:157:12050:17:17:82:403:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:correlations in the data are broadly consistent with this prediction.
5:158:12119:17:17:99:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Finally, we examine the roll-call votes in the Senate on the legislation for changing the Con-
5:159:12213:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:stitution to remove the one-term limit and allow presidential re-election to illustrate a possible
5:160:12311:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:channel for the `quid pro quo' between legislators elected from high paramilitary areas and the
5:161:12406:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:executive. We \fnd evidence that the greater was the proportion of votes a senator's list obtained
5:162:12504:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in high paramilitary areas, the greater was the likelihood of the senator to vote in favor of remov-
5:163:12604:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ing the term limit. Column 2 of Table 1 shows that of those who voted all but three of our `top
5:164:12699:17:17:82:281:282:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:20' senators voted in favor of re-election.3
5:165:12743:17:17:99:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our econometric analysis proceeds under the assumption that our measures of the presence of
5:166:12834:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries and guerillas are exogenous. We are therefore cautious about giving causal inter-
5:167:12930:17:15:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:pretations to the conditional correlations we uncover. For example, it may be that paramilitaries
5:168:13027:15:15:95:543:216:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:1These clauses, supported by President Uribe, reduced the penalties that could be applied to former combatants
5:169:13137:15:11:82:543:201:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:and removed the possibility of extraditing them (to the United States). They were deemed to be `pro-paramilitary'
5:170:13250:11:7:82:543:190:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:by international legal analysts and human rights NGOs, such as Human Rights Watch and Amnesty International.
5:171:13358:7:15:95:543:183:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:2Table 1 uses our main measures of paramilitary presence using data on attacks and con\rict incidents. Appendix
5:172:13469:15:7:82:509:168:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Table A1 reproduces Table 1 using a di-erent measure of paramilitary presence, with very similar results.
5:173:13574:7:15:95:543:161:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:3There is no direct evidence that President Uribe is in some formal `coalition' with paramilitaries, and we do not
5:174:13688:15:11:82:543:146:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:argue or believe that he is; in fact, the politicians in our theoretical model are not in such a coalition either. What
5:175:13807:11:11:82:543:135:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:matters is that President Uribe's relatively conservative policies are closer to those preferred by the paramilitaries,
5:176:13926:11:11:82:543:124:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:who have strong conservative leanings and thus naturally have an interest in maintaining him in power. Some of
5:177:14036:11:11:82:543:113:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:our theoretical and empirical results then exploit the fact that he may take this into account in several of his key
5:178:14152:11:0:82:120:102:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:decisions.
6:179:14163:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:select into areas where people's preferences are `conservative' and would naturally support the new
6:180:14262:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:`third parties' or President Uribe, thus creating a positive association between these variables and
6:181:14362:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary presence. Nevertheless, most of our \fndings come from panel data models with \fxed
6:182:14458:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:e-ects, so that if there are time-invariant di-erences in political preferences across municipalities,
6:183:14560:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:these will not in\ruence our results.  In addition, we use direct controls for how `conservative'
6:184:14657:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:di-erent municipalities are, and as already mentioned above, in the regressions on the persistence
6:185:14755:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the paramilitaries over time, we see paramilitaries persist precisely in places which, in the ab-
6:186:14855:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sence of paramilitary coercion, were relatively unlikely to have voted for President Uribe. Finally,
6:187:14955:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the fact that paramilitary presence predicts the arrests of senators suggests that politicians are
6:188:15053:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:not simply the perfect agents of underlying voter preferences, but are in fact implicated with the
6:189:15151:17:17:82:396:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:non-state armed actors, as the case study literature also suggests.
6:190:15218:17:17:99:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our empirical evidence comes from a speci\fc country, Colombia; we must thus exercise caution
6:191:15311:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in making claims about external validity.4Nonetheless, we believe the political mechanisms
6:192:15401:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:emphasized in this paper are useful in building a richer political explanation for why many modern
6:193:15499:17:17:82:544:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(and in fact democratic) states do not establish a monopoly of violence in their territory.5At the
6:194:15597:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:very least, the theoretical ideas and the empirical evidence presented here show that the implicit
6:195:15695:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:notion that `modernization' in less-developed economies will naturally lead to the formation of
6:196:15790:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a Weberian state, mimicking the European experience, needs to be revised, re\fned or perhaps
6:197:15882:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:even abandoned. Colombia has experienced over a century of sustained increases in GDP per-
6:198:15972:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:capita, large increases in educational attainment, rapid urbanization, indeed all of the features of
6:199:16072:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:modernization (Robinson and Urrutia ed., 2007). Yet the state has not established a monopoly
6:200:16164:17:17:82:135:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of violence.
6:201:16176:17:18:99:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In addition to the literature cited above, the arguments in this paper are related to the recent
6:202:16272:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:political economy literature on the determinants of state capacity. For example, Acemoglu (2005)
6:203:16368:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:conceptualizes state capacity as the ability to tax citizens, and examines the consequences of
6:204:16462:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:state capacity for economic growth and welfare. Acemoglu, Ticchi and Vindigni (2006) model the
6:205:16556:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:endogenous creation of capacity by an elite facing democratization. They argue that the elite may
6:206:16653:17:15:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:have an incentive to choose ine-cient state institutions to limit the amount of redistribution they
6:207:16752:15:15:95:543:233:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:4It can also be argued that the political equilibrium of the last decade in Colombia will ultimately pave the way
6:208:16865:15:11:82:543:218:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:to a modern Weberian state. Whether this is the case or not has no direct bearing on our analysis. Nevertheless,
6:209:16977:11:11:82:543:207:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:we suspect that the symbiotic relationship between the executive and non-state armed groups is not a transient
6:210:17087:11:11:82:543:196:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:phenomenon. Chaves, Fergusson and Robinson (2009) show that the outcome of the 1922 Presidential election
6:211:17192:11:11:82:543:185:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:was determined by fraud and violence with regional patterns strikingly similar to those seen in 2002 or 2006. In
6:212:17304:11:11:82:543:174:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:this light, the mechanisms we isolate here may be the most recent incarnation of a process whose roots lie deep
6:213:17415:11:11:82:543:163:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:in Colombian history. In this interpretation, it may have been the prior absence of state presence and authority
6:214:17527:11:11:82:543:152:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:that led to the formation of the AUC in the \frst place, but in doing so it may have reproduced the same historical
6:215:17642:11:7:82:162:141:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:pattern of behavior.
6:216:17662:7:15:95:543:134:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:5Naturally, it is possible that the mechanism that we identify here may be less important in non-democratic
6:217:17769:15:11:82:543:119:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:regimes, though even dictators require support. Recall, for example, that as noted above it was General Musharraf,
6:218:17883:11:11:82:543:108:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:not any of the democratic Pakistani governments, who increased the number of representatives of the tribal areas
6:219:17995:11:0:82:186:97:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:in the National Assembly.
7:220:18021:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:will face under democracy. In a related paper, Besley and Persson (2009) develop a model where
7:221:18115:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:politicians have to decide whether to build \fscal capacity. None of these papers are concerned
7:222:18210:17:17:82:491:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with the issue of establishing a monopoly of violence, which is the focus of our paper.
7:223:18297:17:17:99:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Within political science our work relates to the literature on `subnational authoritarianism'
7:224:18390:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which has emphasized how democratization at the national level can coexist with highly author-
7:225:18484:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:itarian local practices (O'Donnell, 1993, Gibson, 2005, Mickey, 2009). This research has given
7:226:18578:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:examples of some of the mechanisms contained in our model, but has not developed these ideas
7:227:18670:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:formally, has not noticed the key predictions that our model develops, or provided an econometric
7:228:18767:17:17:82:213:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:investigation of these ideas.
7:229:18796:17:17:99:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The literature on civil war addresses some of the issues we emphasize here implicitly, for
7:230:18886:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:example, in its stress on the weakness of the state (e.g., Fearon and Laitin, 2003). Nevertheless,
7:231:18984:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:most of the research on civil war focuses on the motivations which lie behind the decisions of
7:232:19078:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:people to take up arms against their governments (see, e.g., the excellent survey by Blattman,
7:233:19172:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Miguel, 2008). In this work the fact that a state does not have a monopoly of violence arises
7:234:19269:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:because given the expected bene\ft of allocating resources to \fghting rebels or insurgents, it is not
7:235:19371:17:17:82:291:453:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:worth paying the cost of eliminating them.6
7:236:19414:17:17:99:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our work owes a great debt to the journalists, scholars and public o-cials who have played key
7:237:19508:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:roles in bringing to light the involvement of paramilitaries and the AUC in politics in Colombia.
7:238:19605:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Particularly important has been the work of the researchers whose essays appear in Romero
7:239:19694:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(2007). S-anchez and Palau (2006) also show that political competition is negatively correlated
7:240:19789:17:17:82:320:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with murders of politicians in municipal elections.
7:241:19840:17:17:99:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The paper proceeds as follows. In the next section we develop a theoretical model to examine
7:242:19932:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the incentives of politicians controlling the central state to eliminate or live with non-state armed
7:243:20033:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:actors depending on whether they receive electoral support from these groups. Section 3 provides
7:244:20129:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a brief overview of the history and nature of non-state armed actors in Colombia.  Section 4
7:245:20221:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:describes the data we use and provides some basic descriptive statistics.  Section 5 provides
7:246:20314:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:regression evidence consistent with the e-ects of paramilitaries on electoral outcomes. Section 6
7:247:20411:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:examines the key prediction of our theoretical model, that paramilitaries should persist more in
7:248:20507:17:17:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:areas where they deliver votes to the executive and where they would not have otherwise done
7:249:20599:17:17:82:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:as well. Section 7 provides some suggestive evidence on another implication of our model, the
7:250:20692:17:16:82:508:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:symbiotic relationship between the executive and the paramilitaries. Section 8 concludes.
7:251:20781:16:14:95:543:181:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:6There is also a large literature about the origins of con\rict in Colombia (see Bergquist, Pe~naranda, S-anchez
7:252:20893:14:11:82:543:167:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:eds. 1992, 2001, Deas, 1999, and Posada Carb-o, 2003). In\ruenced by the wider academic literature on civil wars,
7:253:21006:11:11:82:543:156:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:this work has emphasized the importance of state weakness in the Colombian context as well (e.g., Waldmann,
7:254:21113:11:11:82:543:145:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:2007). We do not deny that this is important, for example with respect to the persistence of the FARC. Instead,
7:255:21224:11:11:82:543:134:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:we emphasize that state weakness in Colombia is not simply about inability to eliminate non-state armed actors;
7:256:21335:11:0:82:268:123:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:it is also about the lack of incentives to do so.
8:257:21385:0:28:82:151:708:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2  Model
8:258:21393:28:17:82:543:680:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In this section, we present a simple model to formalize the possible channels of interaction be-
8:259:21489:17:17:82:543:663:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tween central government and paramilitaries.7Motivated by the Colombian experience, our focus
8:260:21582:17:17:82:543:646:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:will be on democratic politics, where an incumbent is facing reelection and decides whether to
8:261:21676:17:17:82:543:629:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reconquer some of the areas under paramilitary control. The model will highlight how paramili-
8:262:21770:17:17:82:543:612:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tary preferences in\ruence electoral outcomes because paramilitaries can coerce voters to support
8:263:21867:17:17:82:543:595:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:one candidate over another. It will then show how the e-ect of paramilitaries on electoral out-
8:264:21962:17:17:82:543:578:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:comes in\ruences the willingness of the democratic central government to reconquer and remove
8:265:22055:17:17:82:543:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the paramilitaries from di-erent areas|the conditions of the formation of the modern Weberian
8:266:22148:17:17:82:543:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:state with a monopoly of violence over the entire country. Finally, we also investigate how the
8:267:22243:17:17:82:543:527:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence of paramilitaries a-ects the policy choices of the party in power.  Our purpose is to
8:268:22337:17:17:82:543:510:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:communicate the main ideas in the simplest possible way. Our empirical work will then provide
8:269:22430:17:17:82:543:493:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:evidence showing how paramilitaries in\ruence electoral outcomes and how this e-ect on elections
8:270:22526:17:17:82:384:476:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:interacts with the persistence of paramilitaries in certain areas.
8:271:22592:17:17:99:543:459:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We consider a two-period model of political competition between two parties.  PartyAis
8:272:22678:17:17:82:543:442:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:initially (att= 0) in power and att= 1, it competes in an election against partyB. The country
8:273:22772:17:17:82:543:425:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:consists of a large equal-sized number,N, of regions, with each region inhabited by a large number
8:274:22870:17:17:82:543:408:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of individuals. We denote the collection of these regions byN. The party that wins the majority
8:275:22965:17:17:82:543:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the votes over all regions wins the election att= 1.8Regions di-er in terms of their policy and
8:276:23063:17:17:82:543:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ideological preferences and, in addition, some regions are under paramilitary control. We assume
8:277:23159:17:17:82:543:357:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:as in standard Downsian models that parties can make commitments to their policies, but their
8:278:23252:17:17:82:543:340:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ideological stance is \fxed (and may capture dimensions of policies to which they cannot make
8:279:23345:17:30:82:153:323:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:commitments).
8:280:23358:30:24:82:380:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.1  Electoral Competition without Paramilitaries
8:281:23407:24:17:82:543:269:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We \frst introduce the details of electoral competition at datet= 1 and then return to the
8:282:23497:17:17:82:543:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:decisions att= 0, in particular, to those concerning whether the government in power will
8:283:23586:17:17:82:543:235:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:expend the resources to reconquer some of the territories under paramilitary control. To start
8:284:23680:17:17:82:543:218:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with, let us ignore the regions that are under paramilitary control (these will be introduced below).
8:285:23781:17:16:99:543:201:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The utility of individualiin regionj2N(i.e.j= 1; :::; N) when partyg2fA; Bgis in
8:286:23861:16:15:95:543:185:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:7In the empirical work we examine the impact of both the paramilitaries and the FARC on elections. However,
8:287:23968:15:11:82:543:170:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:since we do not \fnd robust e-ects of the FARC and since case study evidence suggests that the FARC was much
8:288:24076:11:11:82:543:159:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:less involved in electoral politics, in the theoretical model we focus on the relationship between politicians and the
8:289:24194:11:7:82:309:148:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:paramilitaries. We return to this issue in subsection 2.5.
8:290:24252:7:15:95:543:141:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:8This implies that we are looking at a \presidential system," though the empirical evidence below comes mostly
8:291:24362:15:11:82:543:126:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:from votes for senators and congressmen. Focusing on the presidential system simpli\fes the argument without any
8:292:24474:11:0:82:214:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:major implications for our focus.
9:293:24508:0:17:82:165:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:power is given by

13:572:34715:24:17:99:543:661:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This proposition is an important result of our analysis and will be investigated in our empirical
13:573:34812:17:17:82:543:644:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:work. It implies that the willingness of the state to reconquer areas controlled by the paramili-

13:582:35669:17:17:82:543:491:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f4:is,areas that would have otherwise voted for partyB, but paramilitaries are forcing citizens to
13:583:35764:17:17:82:543:474:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f2:vote in favor of partyA. A government that does not require electoral support (e.g., a \purely
13:584:35858:17:17:82:543:457:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:non-democratic" government) would have decided to reconquer all areas with\rj>0. Therefore,
13:585:35949:17:17:82:543:440:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to the extent that-E[-jjj2J]<E[mjjj2Z], i.e., to the extent that paramilitaries are ide-
13:586:36037:17:17:82:543:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ologically closer to the government in power than the opposition party, a democratic government
13:587:36132:17:17:82:543:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:may be less willing to broadcast its power and reconquer areas under paramilitary control than
13:588:36226:17:17:82:486:389:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:such a non-democratic government (or a government that is secure in its position).11
13:589:36310:17:17:99:543:372:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Note an important implication of the functional form assumptions we have imposed so far,
13:590:36398:17:17:82:543:355:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in particular the uniform distributions of idiosyncratic preference and valance terms: the value
13:591:36494:17:17:82:543:338:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of additional votes to the party in power is constant and independent of its \expected winning
13:592:36588:17:17:82:543:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:probability". As a consequence, Proposition 3 takes a simple form, where the value of paramilitary
13:593:36686:17:17:82:543:304:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:votes to the party in power is independent of this probability. With other functional forms, as
13:594:36781:17:17:82:543:287:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in reality, this value, and thus the behavior of this party towards the paramilitary groups, may
13:595:36877:17:17:82:543:270:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:depend on its expected winning probability, for example, making it less responsive to the votes
13:596:36972:17:29:82:510:253:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:delivered by these paramilitary forces when it is ex ante more likely to win the election.12
13:597:37064:29:24:82:543:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.4  Electoral Competition under Paramilitaries with Endogenous Preferences

15:721:40595:28:0:205:319:590:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f2:allj2Zsuch that\rj+

15:727:40650:28:0:200:324:534:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f2:anyj2Zsuch that\rj+
15:728:40669:0:12:327:334:546:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:-
15:729:40670:12:0:333:377:534:11:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f10:--j-^-^-j
15:730:40679:0:12:379:386:546:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:-
15:731:40680:12:29:387:425:534:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:RA<0:
15:732:40685:29:17:99:543:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There are several new features in this proposition.  First, when paramilitaries adjust their
15:733:40777:17:17:82:543:488:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:support depending on the policies and ideological stance of the two parties, the parties then
15:734:40870:17:17:82:543:471:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:change their policies in order to be more attractive to the paramilitaries' policy preferences.
15:735:40965:17:17:82:543:454:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:That is, rather than catering to the preferences of the citizens in the areas that are controlled
15:736:41062:17:17:82:543:437:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by the paramilitaries (which they would have done without the paramilitaries), parties appease
15:737:41156:17:17:82:543:420:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the paramilitaries themselves.  This result is the basis of the potentialsymbioticrelationship
15:738:41250:17:17:82:543:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between paramilitaries and the executive mentioned in the Introduction. Moreover, it can further
15:739:41346:17:17:82:543:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:increase the inequality among the regions, with the policies chosen speci\fcally to support, or
15:740:41441:17:17:82:543:369:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:refrain from threatening, the paramilitaries and the areas where the paramilitaries are strongest.
15:741:41539:17:17:82:543:352:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Two features determine how slanted towards the paramilitaries equilibrium policies are. These
15:742:41632:17:17:82:543:335:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are: the size of the paramilitary-controlled areas (the greater isz, the more in\ruential are the
15:743:41729:17:17:82:543:318:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries in shaping equilibrium policy) and the relative responsiveness of the paramilitaries
15:744:41828:17:17:82:543:301:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to policy concessions (the greater is^-relative to-, the more responsive are policies to paramilitary
15:745:41929:17:17:82:543:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:preferences relative to citizen preferences).  In addition, because electoral competition makes
15:746:42024:17:17:82:543:267:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:both parties cater to the wishes of the paramilitaries, at the end the paramilitaries ideological
15:747:42121:17:17:82:543:250:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:preferences play a central role in whether they force the population to vote for partyAor party
15:748:42216:17:17:82:102:233:11:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f5:B.13
15:749:42220:17:17:99:543:216:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Finally, we can also allow both parties or one of the parties to modify its ideological stance
15:750:42314:17:17:82:543:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(in a credible fashion). The same analysis as here will then imply that in order to attract votes
15:751:42411:17:17:82:543:182:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:from paramilitary-controlled areas, one or both parties may decide to pander to the ideological
15:752:42506:17:16:82:238:165:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:preferences of the paramilitaries.
15:753:42540:16:15:91:543:149:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:13The result that both parties modify their policies to partly cater to the wishes of the paramilitaries has an
15:754:42651:15:11:82:543:134:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:obvious similarity, and an identical mathematical logic, to Baron's (1994) result concerning the e-ects of a lobby
15:755:42765:11:0:82:254:123:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:on the platforms of two competing parties.
16:756:42809:0:24:82:345:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.5  Importance of Non-National Ambitions
16:757:42850:24:17:82:543:684:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:An important question in the context of Colombian politics is why right-wing paramilitary groups
16:758:42946:17:17:82:543:667:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:have become more involved in in\ruencing elections than left-wing guerrillas, in particular, more so
16:759:43046:17:17:82:543:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:than the relatively well-organized FARC. One possible answer is that in contrast to the guerrillas,
16:760:43145:17:17:82:543:633:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the paramilitaries do not have national ambitions, making a coalition between them and the
16:761:43235:17:17:82:543:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:executive controlling the central state more feasible. The model presented so far has implicitly
16:762:43331:17:17:82:543:599:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:made this assumption, since we did not introduce the risk that the non-state armed actors may
16:763:43424:17:17:82:210:582:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:take over the central state.
16:764:43452:17:17:99:543:565:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A simple way of introducing this possibility would be to have a probability \b(z) that the non-
16:765:43547:17:17:82:543:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:state armed actors would become strong enough to challenge the central state, perhaps overthrow
16:766:43642:17:17:82:543:531:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:it. Such an overthrow of the central government by non-state armed actors is not uncommon in
16:767:43734:17:17:82:543:514:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:weak African states, such as Somalia, Sierra Leone or Liberia, and has certainly been the objective
16:768:43833:17:17:82:543:497:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the FARC. Naturally, we would expect \b(z) to be increasing inz, so that when these groups
16:769:43926:17:17:82:543:480:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:control more areas, they are more likely to pose such a national challenge. In that case, we would
16:770:44024:17:17:82:543:463:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:need to change the objective function of partyAto incorporate this possibility. For example,
16:771:44116:17:18:82:242:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:equation (5) could be modi\fed to
16:772:44149:18:24:222:238:428:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:X
16:773:44150:24:0:221:238:404:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f14:j2R
16:774:44153:0:0:240:326:418:11:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f10:\rj+ [1-\b(z)]PA
16:775:44169:0:8:329:334:426:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:-
16:776:44170:8:0:334:379:418:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f13:qA; qBj-
16:777:44178:0:8:379:384:426:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:-
16:778:44179:8:36:386:404:418:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:RA:
16:779:44182:36:18:82:543:382:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This speci\fcation makes it clear that when \b(z)>0, there will be stronger incentives for party
16:780:44278:18:17:82:543:364:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:Ato reconquer territories controlled by these non-state armed groups (thus reducingz). When
16:781:44369:17:17:82:543:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\b(z) is su-ciently high and su-ciently decreasing inz, this e-ect can more than compensate for
16:782:44464:17:17:82:543:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the electoral advantage that local control by these groups creates for the party in power. Thus
16:783:44559:17:17:82:543:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:factoring in the national ambitions of non-state armed actors reduces the room for a coalition
16:784:44653:17:17:82:543:296:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:or a symbiotic relationship between these groups and the executive. Expressed di-erently, this
16:785:44747:17:17:82:543:279:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reasoning suggests that when non-state armed actors have national ambitions, it will be advanta-
16:786:44843:17:17:82:543:262:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:geous for the central state to eliminate them (sooner or later), thus any implicit or explicit policy
16:787:44944:17:17:82:543:245:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:promises that it makes to such groups would be non-credible, making a coalition between them
16:788:45036:17:17:82:543:228:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impossible. This perspective suggests a natural reason for why, in Colombia, such a coalition may
16:789:45133:17:17:82:543:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:have been much more likely to arise between the executive and the paramilitaries rather than
16:790:45225:17:29:82:158:194:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with the FARC.
16:791:45239:29:24:82:327:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.6  Summary and Empirical Predictions
16:792:45277:24:17:82:543:141:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the rest of the paper, we will investigate the e-ect of Colombian paramilitary forces on the
16:793:45372:17:17:82:543:124:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:electoral outcomes in the early 2000s. Our investigation is motivated by the theoretical ideas
16:794:45466:17:17:82:543:107:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:discussed above. In particular, we will document the following broad patterns, which, though not
16:795:45562:17:0:82:400:90:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:conclusive proof of the ideas developed here, are highly suggestive.
17:796:45632:0:17:96:544:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1. Consistent with Proposition 2, paramilitaries, once they became su-ciently powerful, started
17:797:45727:17:26:110:452:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in\ruencing electoral outcomes in the areas of Colombia they controlled.
17:798:45799:26:17:96:543:665:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2. Consistent with Proposition 3, we will show that paramilitaries located in areas that voted
17:799:45893:17:17:110:544:648:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:for the current President in great numbers, but in past elections tended to vote for more
17:800:45982:17:26:110:321:631:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:liberal politicians, are more likely to persist.
17:801:46030:26:17:96:543:605:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:3. Consistent with Proposition 4, we will show that the President has proposed legislation in
17:802:46123:17:17:110:544:588:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:line with the preferences of the paramilitaries, and the Senators elected from high paramil-
17:803:46215:17:35:110:313:571:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:itary areas have supported this legislation.
17:804:46259:35:24:82:523:536:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3  A Brief Overview of Non-State Armed Actors in Colombia
17:805:46316:24:24:82:391:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.1  Origins of Colombian Non-State Armed Actors
17:806:46364:24:17:82:543:488:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Colombia has a long history of non-state armed actors. During the 19th century the country was
17:807:46458:17:18:82:543:471:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:convulsed by a series of civil wars which culminated in the War of Thousand Days between 1899
17:808:46551:18:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and 1902 (see Pardo, 2004, for an overview).  Relative peace emerged subsequently (Mazzuca
17:809:46641:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Robinson, 2009) and lasted until the 1940s when the country again slipped into a murderous
17:810:46735:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:civil war known asLa Violencia,which slowly came to a halt after 1958 when the Liberal and
17:811:46825:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Conservative parties signed a peace treaty and re-established elections, albeit under a highly
17:812:46919:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:restrictive set of power sharing institutions known as the National Front (see Guzm-an Campos,
17:813:47013:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f4:Fals Borda and Uma~na Luna, 1962, Oquist, 1980, P-ecaut, 2001, Rold-an, 2002 onLa Violencia
17:814:47104:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Hartlyn, 1988, on the National Front). Though the National Front brought to an end the 100
17:815:47198:17:17:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:year con\rict between the Liberal and Conservative parties, it issued in multifarious new forms
17:816:47293:17:17:82:543:317:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of con\rict.  In 1964 out of the ashes of various Liberal and Communist guerillas, was formed
17:817:47386:17:17:82:543:300:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the Fuerzas Armadas Revolucionarias de Colombia (FARC|The Revolutionary Armed Forces
17:818:47470:17:17:82:543:283:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Colombia). In the same year the Ej-ercito de Liberaci-on Nacional (ELN|National Liberation
17:819:47563:17:17:82:543:266:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Army) was also created. These `left-wing' guerilla groups were relatively small during the 1960s
17:820:47659:17:17:82:543:249:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and 1970s, but began to expand rapidly in the 1980s and they were joined by other left-wing
17:821:47750:17:17:82:543:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:revolutionary movements such as the Movimiento 19 de Abril (M-19|Movement of April 19)
17:822:47836:17:17:82:543:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and Quint--n Lame. The 1980s also saw the rapid expansion of `right-wing' paramilitary forces
17:823:47929:17:17:82:543:198:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which in 1997 coalesced into the Autodefensas Unidas de Colombia (AUC|United Self-Defense
17:824:48018:17:17:82:212:181:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Organization of Colombia).
17:825:48044:17:17:99:543:164:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:These various non-state armed groups ranged over most of the territory of Colombia and
17:826:48130:17:17:82:543:147:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:though estimates vary, may have had around 50,000 men and women under arms at the start
17:827:48217:17:17:82:543:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the 21st Century. They engaged in kidnapping, massacres of civilians, drug production and
17:828:48309:17:17:82:543:113:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:exportation, and regularly expropriated land and extorted income (`collected the taxes') from
17:829:48402:17:0:82:543:96:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Colombian citizens. They also engaged in violent con\ricts with each other and with the armed
18:830:48497:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:forces of the Colombian state. Map 1 in the Appendix shows the distribution of the FARC/ELN
18:831:48588:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and the AUC across Colombia's 1,119 municipalities (using the `attacks' data, described below,
18:832:48682:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:over the period 1997-2005).  The map uses di-erent shades of red to indicate municipalities
18:833:48773:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in di-erent quintiles of the distribution of guerrilla presence.  The darkest red indicates the
18:834:48868:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:20% of places with the most intense guerilla activity.  One can see that this covers most of
18:835:48960:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Colombia. Departments in the eastern planes (`Los Llanos'), such as Arauca and Casanare, have
18:836:49053:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:high guerilla presence as do municipalities further south in Caquet-a, where the negotiations took
18:837:49151:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:place during the Presidency of Andr-es Pastrana.  However, high guerilla presence can also be
18:838:49244:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:seen in the Northeast, in the department of Norte de Santander, further west in Antioquia and
18:839:49337:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the southwest in Cauca. Map 2 in the Appendix examines paramilitary presence using the
18:840:49426:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:same data. One sees high paramilitary presence, measured in the same way as for the guerilla,
18:841:49519:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in many of the same areas. These include the eastern planes, Norte de Santander and Antioquia.
18:842:49613:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Paramilitary presence is also high in municipalities in the coastal department of Magdalena and
18:843:49708:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in C-esar, inbetween Magdalena and Norte de Santander.  This is natural, since paramilitaries
18:844:49801:17:30:82:295:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:often formed to \fght the left-wing guerrillas.
18:845:49848:30:24:82:279:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.2  Paramilitaries and the AUC
18:846:49879:24:17:82:543:416:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Colombia's paramilitaries are thought to originate from 1960s counterinsurgency measures and
18:847:49971:17:17:82:543:399:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Law 48 of 1968 which allowed the creation of self-defense militias by private citizens for the
18:848:50065:17:17:82:543:382:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:purposes of protecting their properties and lives (see Romero, 2000, 2002, Rangel, 2005, and
18:849:50157:17:17:82:543:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Duncan, 2007, for overviews of the history and organization of the paramilitaries). Nevertheless,
18:850:50254:17:17:82:543:348:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the period ofLa Violenciais littered with various sorts of militias and spontaneous self-defense
18:851:50350:17:17:82:543:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:groups (see Rold-an, 2002, on Antioquia). Small groups of paramilitaries also emerged in places
18:852:50445:17:17:82:543:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:where there were valuable resources whose exploitation was contested such as in the emerald
18:853:50536:17:17:82:543:297:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mines of Muzo, in the department of Boyac-a and the drug plantations on the coast near Santa
18:854:50628:17:17:82:389:280:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Marta, Magdalena and in the nearby department of La Guajira.
18:855:50688:17:17:99:543:263:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The escalation of paramilitaries in the early 1980s is associated with the rise of the large drug
18:856:50785:17:17:82:543:246:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:cartels in Medell--n and Cali that faced threats of kidnapping and extortion from left-wing groups.
18:857:50884:17:17:82:543:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In 1981 Martha Nieves Ochoa, the sister of Jorge Luis Ochoa V-azquez, one of the founders of the
18:858:50980:17:17:82:543:212:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Medell--n drug cartel (along with his brothers, Pablo Escobar, Carlos Lehder and Jos-e Gonzalo
18:859:51074:17:17:82:543:195:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Rodr--guez Gacha), was kidnapped by the guerilla group M-19. In retaliation, the cartel formed an
18:860:51171:17:17:82:543:178:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:armed paramilitary group called Muerte a Secuestradores (MAS|Death to Kidnappers) whose
18:861:51258:17:17:82:240:161:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:aim was to eliminate kidnappers.
18:862:51290:17:17:99:543:144:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:As the wealth of the drug cartels grew, many of their members began to buy up land and
18:863:51376:17:17:82:543:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ranches in rural areas. Here their interests began to fuse with those of traditional rural elites who
18:864:51477:17:17:82:543:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:also wished to protect themselves from extortion and kidnappers (see Guti-errez San--n and Bar-on,
18:865:51575:17:0:82:543:93:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2005, for a study of this process in the Puerto Boyac-a region). This led to collaboration in the
19:866:51674:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:formation of paramilitary groups. One area of rapid expansion was the Magdalena Medio at the
19:867:51766:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:eastern periphery of the department of Antioquia which saw the emergence of groups such as Los
19:868:51860:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Tangueros formed by the Casta~no brothers (Carlos, Fidel and Vicente). Five of Carlos Casta~no's
19:869:51956:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:11 siblings were killed by guerrillas, following the abduction and death of their dairy-farmer father,
19:870:52058:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Jesus Casta~no, in 1981. In 1981, FARC snatched the Casta~no's father and demanded a $7,500
19:871:52149:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ransom, which was raised by mortgaging the farm. Though the ransom was paid, the father's
19:872:52238:17:17:82:490:606:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:corpse was found chained to a tree. Los Tangueros was founded to revenge this act.14
19:873:52322:17:17:99:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In 1992 people who had been victimized by the drug lord Pablo Escobar founded a paramilitary
19:874:52414:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:organization called `Los Pepes' (`Perseguidos por Pablo Escobar'|those persecuted by Pablo
19:875:52504:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Escobar). This group, which played an important informal role in the hunt for Escobar and his
19:876:52597:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:death in 1993 (Bowden, 2002) apparently included all of the Casta~no brothers, even though they
19:877:52692:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:had previously cooperated with the Medell--n cartel. In 1994 the brothers formed the `Autodefensas
19:878:52790:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Campesinas de C-ordoba y Urab-a' (ACCU|Peasant Self-Defense force of C-ordoba and Urab-a).
19:879:52880:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This further expansion was facilitated in the same year by a law promoted by President Samper
19:880:52973:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to allow the creation of CONVIVIR, a national program of neighborhood watch groups.  An
19:881:53060:17:17:82:544:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:important supported of this program was-Alvaro Uribe, then Governor of Antioquia, whose father
19:882:53154:17:17:82:199:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:was killed by the FARC.
19:883:53177:17:17:99:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In April 1997 the AUC was formed by Carlos Casta~no and it included possibly 90% of the
19:884:53264:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:existing paramilitary forces. The creation of this national organization increased the e-ectiveness
19:885:53363:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the paramilitaries considerably; as a result, the FARC and ELN were thrown out of large areas
19:886:53459:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the country, though as our data will show these guerrilla groups are still active in many parts
19:887:53557:17:17:82:348:351:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:of Colombia (see Restrepo, Spagat and Vargas, 2004).15
19:888:53611:17:18:99:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Soon after coming to power in 2002, President Uribe began to negotiate the demobilization of
19:889:53703:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the paramilitaries, something he had promised during his election campaign. Decree 128 issued by
19:890:53799:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the President in January 2003 gave de facto amnesty for paramilitaries not under investigation for
19:891:53897:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:human rights violations and this has been applied to the vast number of demobilizations (around
19:892:53992:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:92%). On July 15, 2003 in Santa F-e de Ralito in C-ordoba the government signed an agreement
19:893:54084:17:17:82:408:248:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:with most of the groups of the AUC to disarm by the end of 2005.16
19:894:54150:17:17:99:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:On November 25 2003 around 860 paramilitaries of Medell--n's Cacique Nutibara Bloc led by
19:895:54239:17:17:82:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:`Don Berna' (Diego Fernando Murillo) demobilized. This process was further institutionalized by
19:896:54334:17:16:82:543:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the passing of the controversial Justice and Peace Law in June 2005 which was signed into law
19:897:54427:16:14:91:543:181:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:14There is also evidence suggesting involvement of the army in the training and organization of paramilitary
19:898:54535:14:11:82:543:167:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:groups, though in 1989 the Colombian Supreme Court declared that Law 48 was unconstitutional. One month later
19:899:54644:11:11:82:543:156:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:President Barco issued Decree 1194 which prohibited the creation, promotion or organization of paramilitary or
19:900:54754:11:7:82:300:145:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:self-defense groups and declared such activities illegal.
19:901:54811:7:15:91:543:138:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:15The timing of the creation of the AUC was a consequence of the collapse of the Medell--n and Cali drug cartels
19:902:54923:15:7:82:406:123:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:which had previously exercised a large amount of control over the organizations.
19:903:55003:7:15:91:543:116:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:16The text of the agreement is available at the web page of the O-ce of the High Commissioner for Peace:
19:904:55107:15:0:82:320:101:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:www.altocomisionadoparalapaz.gov.co/acuerdos/index.htm
20:905:55163:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by President Uribe in the following month. Article 29 of this law limits sentences to those found
20:906:55260:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:guilty of human rights violations to between 5 and 8 years. Article 30 allows the government to
20:907:55355:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:determine the place of detention, which need not be a prison. In May 2006 the Colombian Con-
20:908:55447:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:stitutional Court altered many aspects of the law on the grounds that they were unconstitutional,
20:909:55544:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in particular the Court stipulated that demobilizing combatants had to give a full confession of
20:910:55640:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:their activities in order for the law to apply to them. Both the demobilization process and the
20:911:55735:17:17:82:478:606:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:Justice and Peace Law have been widely criticized by human rights organization.17
20:912:55816:17:17:99:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There is a great deal of controversy about whether the paramilitary demobilization is real or
20:913:55909:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whether it will lead to new armed groups (or simply to the institutionalization/legitimation of
20:914:56004:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the power of the AUC; on this issue see Pardo, 2007, International Crisis Group, 2007, Porch and
20:915:56100:17:30:82:170:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Rasmussen, 2008).
20:916:56117:30:24:82:377:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.3  The Involvement of Paramilitaries in Politics
20:917:56167:24:17:82:543:484:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Soon after the foundation of the AUC in 1997 there appears to have been a strategic decision to
20:918:56262:17:17:82:543:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in\ruence electoral politics. This change is traced to a historic meeting in Santa F-e de Ralito in
20:919:56361:17:17:82:543:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2001 where members of theestado mayor(the governing body) of the AUC along with politicians
20:920:56452:17:17:82:543:433:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and members of Congress signed a secret document calling for the `refounding of the country'.
20:921:56545:17:17:82:543:416:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Those who signed this document included prominent paramilitary leaders, such as Jorge 40 (Ro-
20:922:56638:17:17:82:543:399:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:drigo Tovar Pupo) and Diego Vecino, and several politicians subsequently arrested for links with
20:923:56734:17:17:82:543:382:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries, including Senators William Montes and Miguel de la Espriella (see Table 1). An
20:924:56828:17:16:82:542:365:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:explicit aim of the accord was to have the AUC play a more important role in electoral politics.18
20:925:56926:16:14:91:543:349:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:17For instance the 2007 report of the International Federation for Human Rights notes: \The paramilitaries who
20:926:57036:14:11:82:543:335:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:do fall under the Justice and Peace Act are tried at so-called \free version" hearings and may be sentenced to
20:927:57146:11:11:82:543:324:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:no more than eight years of imprisonment, which they may serve in \work farms." They may even impose their
20:928:57252:11:11:82:543:313:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:own conditions for \imprisonment," which \ries in the face of the most basic principles of justice in view of the
20:929:57365:11:11:82:543:302:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:seriousness of the crimes committed." The report also emphasizes \the lack of true willingness on the part of the
20:930:57478:11:11:82:543:291:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:government to bring to trial and dismantle the paramilitary groups," and concludes that: \The paramilitaries
20:931:57586:11:11:82:543:280:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:are not forced to confess to their crimes, disclose the truth about who supported their structures, or even show
20:932:57698:11:11:82:543:269:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:repentance for their crimes. They have not been forced to turn in all of their weapons or hand over their assets
20:933:57810:11:11:82:543:258:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:to compensate the victims, while the latter and their representatives have very limited access to hearings and are
20:934:57924:11:11:82:543:247:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:hindered from participating in them....What is more, those victims who have attended the \free version" hearings
20:935:58036:11:11:82:543:236:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:have not received adequate protection. Already, sixteen of them have been murdered with absolute impunity." See
20:936:58147:11:11:82:360:225:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:also Human Rights Watch (2005) and Amnesty International (2005).
20:937:58211:11:11:92:544:214:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:On the issue of handing in weapons the Inter-American Commission on Human Rights (2007) noted at some key
20:938:58316:11:11:82:543:203:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:demobilizations in the department of C-esar that \approximately 800 persons had passed through that circuit on
20:939:58426:11:11:82:543:192:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the previous day, but only 65 \frearms were received. It also noted that from the 200 persons passing through the
20:940:58539:11:11:82:543:181:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:circuit at La Mesa on the previous day, roughly 25 \frearms were received. None of the weapons surrendered were
20:941:58650:11:7:82:231:170:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:modern or in good condition" (p. 8).
20:942:58686:7:15:91:543:163:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:18Although the meeting in Ralito was probably the most important one for the subsequent strategy of the
20:943:58789:15:11:82:543:148:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:paramilitaries, it was not the only such pact between them and politicians during this period. In the southern
20:944:58899:11:11:82:543:137:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:plains, paramilitary leader Hector Buitrago (Martin Llanos) organized a meeting in 2000 with all the candidates
20:945:59010:11:11:82:543:126:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:running for the governor's and the mayor's o-ces and explicitly traded political support against key positions in
20:946:59123:11:11:82:543:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the local executive, allocations of public contracts, and a share in the resources of the municipality (\La Sombra
20:947:59237:11:11:82:543:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:de Martin Llanos" Semana, October 8, 2007). In Puerto Berio, Antioquia, four congressmen from Santander met
20:948:59344:11:0:82:543:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:with paramilitary leader Salvatore Mancuso in 2001 for a similar pact. In the Municipalities of Chivolo and Pivijay
21:949:59461:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This change in the strategy of the AUC will be crucial to our empirical approach, allowing us
21:950:59554:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to investigate how electoral outcomes change di-erentially in high paramilitary areas before and
21:951:59650:17:17:82:283:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:after their involvement in politics in 2001.
21:952:59694:17:17:99:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The other notable, and related, development during the 2002 election is the emergence of
21:953:59782:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:brand new political parties, which we refer to as `third parties,' such as Cambio Radical and
21:954:59875:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:MIPOL. These parties often had explicit or implicit links with the paramilitaries, and the case
21:955:59970:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:study evidence shows that paramilitary pressure was often to increase the vote for these parties.
21:956:60067:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In many paramilitary-controlled areas they have replaced the traditional Liberal and Conservative
21:957:60164:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:parties. We will use the vote share of `third parties' as a measure of paramilitary in\ruence on
21:958:60260:17:17:82:173:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:electoral outcomes.
21:959:60279:17:17:99:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Beginning in 2005 there were increasing accusations of involvement of the AUC in the elections
21:960:60373:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of 2002. Scandal mounted further with the demobilization of Jorge 40 and his 2,000 strong block
21:961:60468:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on March 10, 2006 in La Mesa, C-esar. Jorge 40's computer fell into the hands of government
21:962:60559:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:o-cials and it contained emails ordering his men to recruit peasants to pretend to be paramilitaries
21:963:60659:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:during demobilization ceremonies.19The computer also listed over 500 murders and detailed many
21:964:60753:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:links between politicians and paramilitaries. These accusations led to intense scrutiny of the 2002
21:965:60852:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:election results many of which exhibit some rather extraordinary features. These include massive
21:966:60948:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:changes in voting patterns and very high concentrations of votes for some candidates in particular
21:967:61046:17:17:82:159:402:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:municipalities.20

21:971:61346:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Zabala, 2007 and the web site verdadabierta.com). As of May 29, 2009, 39 members of Congress
21:972:61438:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and the Senate were under investigation, 36 were arrested and in detention, and 11 had been found

23:1060:69247:11:11:82:544:189:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:also how votes were guaranteed.Semanadocumented how paramilitary leaders and politicians divided up coastal
23:1061:69354:11:10:82:543:178:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:departments. For instance: \In C-esar, \Jorge 40" aimed to obtain two Senators and four Representatives. The
23:1062:69462:10:11:82:543:168:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:department was divided into 3 electoral districts, one in the north and one in the south. Each of the candidates
23:1063:69574:11:11:82:543:157:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:would campaign in only one of those districts and each of these would support two candidates for the House of
23:1064:69683:11:11:82:543:146:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Representatives. The third district would be open to free competition. To organize the lists they did everything,
23:1065:69796:11:11:82:543:135:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:from threats and expropriation of land to kidnappings. They killed Luis Laborde, former mayor of Copey and
23:1066:69902:11:11:82:543:124:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:candidate to the House of Representatives, who did not want to \play" the rules of the game that were imposed
23:1067:70011:11:11:82:543:113:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:by the AUC. \\Jorge 40" announced this crime in a meeting in San Angel, in which there were 9 mayors of the
23:1068:70118:11:11:82:543:102:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:department" says a witness. Since that moment it was completely clear that anyone who did not comply with
23:1069:70223:11:0:82:377:91:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:\Jorge 40's" rules could not do politics" (Semana, November 25th 2006).
24:1070:70296:0:30:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:not run against their preferred candidates, and manipulating subsequent vote totals electronically.
24:1071:70395:30:24:82:418:678:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.5  The Involvement of Other Armed Actors in Politics
24:1072:70449:24:17:82:543:654:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our empirical results will show that the AUC more than any non-state armed actor has been
24:1073:70538:17:17:82:543:637:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:signi\fcantly in\ruencing elections in Colombia. Scattered pieces of evidence suggest that other
24:1074:70634:17:17:82:543:620:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:non-state armed actors have been involved, but have not pursued such a consistent electoral
24:1075:70725:17:17:82:543:603:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:strategy. For instance the drug lord Pablo Escobar got himself elected as an alternate for a list to
24:1076:70825:17:17:82:543:586:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Congress in 1982 for the Liberal party and it is very likely that he and members of the Medell--n
24:1077:70922:17:17:82:543:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:drug cartel had big impacts on elections in Antioquia, though to our knowledge the data have
24:1078:71014:17:17:82:543:552:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:never been systematically analyzed. Nevertheless, electoral strategies can be dangerous. Escobar's
24:1079:71112:17:17:82:543:535:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:election drew a lot of attention to him, which was probably not to the advantage of his business
24:1080:71208:17:17:82:543:518:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:interests and no doubt strengthened the resolve of the state to move against him. Similarly in the
24:1081:71306:17:17:82:543:501:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1980s when the FARC formed a party to contest elections, the Uni-on Patri-otica (UP- Patriotic
24:1082:71400:17:17:82:543:484:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Union) many of their supporters and candidates including their Presidential candidates in the
24:1083:71493:17:17:82:272:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1986 and 1990 elections were murdered.
24:1084:71531:17:17:99:543:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The FARC and ELN have also certainly in\ruenced some elections and have used their power
24:1085:71619:17:17:82:543:433:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to sway or intimidate voters in favor of candidates they preferred. They have threatened and
24:1086:71711:17:17:82:543:416:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:killed politicians. However, their involvement in elections has been more limited than that of
24:1087:71805:17:17:82:543:399:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the AUC. We conjecture that this is mostly because the FARC and ELN have been ideologically
24:1088:71896:17:17:82:543:382:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:opposed to the institutions of the state in Colombia and their project was to overthrow the
24:1089:71987:17:17:82:543:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:national government. As also emphasized by our theoretical discussion in subsection 2.5, this
24:1090:72080:17:17:82:543:348:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:made a symbiotic relationship between them and the executive impossible. In contrast, the AUC
24:1091:72173:17:17:82:543:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are a continuation of local paramilitary groups allied with local elites and politicians. Again in
24:1092:72271:17:17:82:543:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:light of our discussion in subsection 2.5, it was important that the AUC did not want to overthrow
24:1093:72369:17:17:82:543:297:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the state but to exercise control over certain peripheral areas and in\ruence key legislation. This
24:1094:72468:17:17:82:543:280:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:created a platform for a symbiotic relationship between the central state and the AUC, which
24:1095:72560:17:29:82:333:263:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:would have been impossible for the FARC and ELN.
24:1096:72608:29:24:82:303:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.6  The Colombian Political System
24:1097:72643:24:17:82:543:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Here we emphasize a few institutional details of the Colombian system that are important for our
24:1098:72739:17:17:82:543:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:empirical strategy. Under the 1991 Constitution the President of Colombia was elected for one
24:1099:72832:17:17:82:543:176:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:four year term with no possibility of re-election. There has been a strong norm against re-election
24:1100:72931:17:17:82:543:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:historically in Colombia and the last President to succeed himself was Rafael N-u~nez in 1886.
24:1101:73025:17:17:82:543:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Though under the 1886 Constitution re-election was permitted if not successive, it only happened
24:1102:73121:17:17:82:543:125:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:once with Alfonso L-opez Pumarejo being President between 1934 and 1938 and again between
24:1103:73210:17:17:82:543:108:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1942 and 1945 (when he ended his second term early by resigning). The President is elected by
24:1104:73303:17:0:82:543:91:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a national vote and if no candidate receives 50% of the vote in the \frst round a run-o- election
25:1105:73402:0:17:82:496:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is held between the two candidates with the largest number of votes in the \frst round.
25:1106:73489:17:17:99:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:It is also important to note that like most Presidential systems in Latin America, Colombia's
25:1107:73582:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:features strong Presidential dominance of the legislature with Presidents often ruling for long
25:1108:73677:17:17:82:208:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:periods by issuing decrees.
25:1109:73704:17:17:99:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For the Senate there is a national constituency where 100 Senators are elected from lists. For
25:1110:73798:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the Congress there are 32 multi-member districts with each district corresponding to a department.
25:1111:73896:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The representation of departments depends on their population and there are 162 Congressmen
25:1112:73987:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in total. Historically in Colombia even traditional party lists are very personalized so the typical
25:1113:74087:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:situation is one where only one candidate is elected from each list. This situation did not change
25:1114:74185:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with the 2006 elections even though a reform in the electoral law stipulated that to win a seat
