25:1115:74280:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the legislature a list had to have at least 2% of the vote nationally.  At the same time as
25:1116:74374:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:this law was introduced, the electoral system was changed to allow for open-list proportional
25:1117:74467:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:representation (with preference voting). Thus even though the number of lists fell dramatically,
25:1118:74563:17:17:82:363:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:personal politics continued unabated via preference voting.
25:1119:74622:17:17:99:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The organization of the Higher Courts in Colombia is rather intricate. There are four High
25:1120:74712:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Courts: the Supreme Court, the Conseil d' Etat (State Council), the Superior Council of the
25:1121:74803:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Judiciary and the Constitutional Court. While the \frst two have been in place since the 1886
25:1122:74896:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Colombian Constitution (although with some alterations), the latter ones were a creation of the
25:1123:74991:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1991 Constitution. For the purposes of paramilitary involvement in politics it is relevant to brie\ry
25:1124:75092:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:understand the basics of the Supreme Court and the Constitutional Court. The Supreme Court's
25:1125:75184:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:main role is to review judgments of inferior (provincial) courts and decide whether there has been
25:1126:75282:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a correct interpretation of the law and/or the facts of the cases. The Court is divided in three
25:1127:75378:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:sections: criminal, civil and labor. The Criminal Section of the Supreme Court is also in charge
25:1128:75474:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of trying and judging \the members of the Congress: Senate and Chamber of Representatives"
25:1129:75564:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(Article 235 # 3 { Constitution). This gives the Supreme Court the authority to judge members
25:1130:75657:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Congress accused of having links with paramilitary groups. Some members of Congress, once
25:1131:75749:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:investigations for paramilitary links have started, have stepped down from their public o-ce to
25:1132:75844:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:avoid the jurisdiction of the Supreme Court and have subjected themselves to ordinary procedures
25:1133:75940:17:17:82:291:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:under \lower-scale" prosecutors and judges.
25:1134:75983:17:17:99:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The Constitutional Court has two types of roles: on the one hand it is in charge of reviewing
25:1135:76076:17:17:82:543:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the judgment of provincial and sectional judges regarding `acciones de tutela,' which is a procedure
25:1136:76176:17:17:82:543:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that any person can start {generally against public o-cials{ in order to seek the protection of
25:1137:76271:17:17:82:543:163:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:his/her fundamental rights. On the other hand the Constitutional Court is in charge of judicial
25:1138:76366:17:17:82:543:146:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:review of legislation. In this role the Court determines whether a particular statute (law enacted by
25:1139:76467:17:17:82:543:129:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Congress) is constitutional. The Constitution provides that some statutes should be automatically
25:1140:76564:17:17:82:543:112:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:reviewed by the Court, while in other cases the Court will only intervene when a citizen challenges
25:1141:76663:17:0:82:543:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the constitutionality of a particular statute.  In the case of the Justice and Peace Law, the
26:1142:76758:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Constitutional Court reviewed its constitutionality thanks to a challenge posed by a group of
26:1143:76851:17:17:82:336:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:citizens (under Article 241 of the 1991 Constitution).
26:1144:76905:17:17:99:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There is a relatively high degree of autonomy of these High Courts vis--a-vis the Executive
26:1145:76996:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Branch, particularly the Supreme Court. There is no life tenure for the Justices in Colombia:
26:1146:77089:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:instead they serve during one eight-year term and re-election to the same court is explicitly
26:1147:77182:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:forbidden by the Constitution. When a Justice serves his time, the Supreme Court is in charge of
26:1148:77278:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:choosing a replacement from lists prepared by the Administrative Section of the Superior Council
26:1149:77374:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the Judiciary (another High Court also in charge of administrative functions regarding the
26:1150:77467:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:judiciary). In turn, the justices of the Administrative Section are appointed by the Constitutional
26:1151:77566:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Court (1 judge), by the Supreme Court (2 judges) and by the Conseil d'Etat (3 judges). The
26:1152:77656:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impact of the legislative and executive branches is therefore very indirect on the Supreme Court.
26:1153:77753:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:They can to some extent in\ruence this process.  For instance the Constitutional Court has 9
26:1154:77845:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:judges elected for life by the Senate. However, the election takes place over lists of candidates
26:1155:77942:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presented by the President (3 judges), the Supreme Court (3 judges) and the Conseil d'Etat (3
26:1156:78035:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:judges). Thus, from the nine justices sitting on the Constitutional Court in a particular term,
26:1157:78130:17:35:82:402:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:three of them have come out from lists presented by the President.
26:1158:78196:35:25:82:173:418:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4  The Data
26:1159:78207:25:24:82:297:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:4.1  Data Sources and Construction
26:1160:78241:24:17:82:543:369:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The most important data for the paper are on the presence of non-state armed actors, speci\fcally
26:1161:78338:17:17:82:543:352:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries and left-wing guerillas. Our main measure of the presence of non-state armed actors
26:1162:78436:17:17:82:543:335:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is one based on con\rict incidents, which we refer to as `attacks' for short. The database of attacks
26:1163:78537:17:17:82:543:318:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is from Centro de Estudios sobre Desarrollo Econ-omico (CEDE) in the Facultad de Econom--a at
26:1164:78630:17:17:82:543:301:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the Universidad de Los Andes in Bogot-a. CEDE collects data from the Observatory of Human
26:1165:78719:17:17:82:543:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Rights of the Vice-presidency and the National Department of Planning and aggregates variables
26:1166:78813:17:17:82:543:267:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in several categories by armed actor and type of action. The original data are a compilation of news
26:1167:78913:17:17:82:543:250:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:from newspapers and from reports of the national police. Our measure ofattacksis constructed
26:1168:79005:17:17:82:543:233:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by aggregating over many of these variables. For each armed actor we simply add the following
26:1169:79098:17:17:82:543:216:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:variables: explosive terrorist acts, incendiary terrorist acts, other terrorist acts, assaults to private
26:1170:79203:17:17:82:543:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:property, attacks on civil organizations, political assassination attempts, road blockades, armed
26:1171:79300:17:17:82:543:182:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:contact between state and non-state armed forces initiated by the latter, ambushes of civilians,
26:1172:79396:17:17:82:543:165:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:harassing (mainly threats to civilians), incursion into `villages', overland piracy, illegal checkpoints,
26:1173:79501:17:17:82:543:148:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:armed forces wounded by the non-state armed group, murders of civilians, murders of politicians,
26:1174:79597:17:17:82:543:131:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:massacres, deaths of members of the state armed forces, kidnappings of members of the armed
26:1175:79688:17:17:82:543:114:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:forces, kidnappings of politicians and kidnappings of civilians. We have this variable for each year
26:1176:79788:17:0:82:211:97:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the period 1997 to 2005.
27:1177:79817:0:17:99:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We check the robustness of our results with an alternative measure of the presence of non-
27:1178:79907:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:state armed actors based on displaced people.  The database from which we constructed our
27:1179:79996:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f2:displacedmeasure comes from Acci-on Social an agency created by the presidency. This data is
27:1180:80088:17:17:82:544:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:collected from people that report themselves and are classi\fed as displaced in the Registro-Unico
27:1181:80186:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:de Poblaci-on Desplazada (unique register of displaced population) in order to obtain a set of
27:1182:80280:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:subsidies. These data specify the municipality where the displacement originated, the year of the
27:1183:80377:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:displacement and the armed actor that originated it. We have these data annually for the period
27:1184:80472:17:17:82:154:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1997 and 2006.
27:1185:80486:17:17:99:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We use these data to construct various measures of the presence of non-state armed actors.
27:1186:80576:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Because the time series variation in both the attacks and the displaced measures appears to be
27:1187:80670:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:quite noisy, we focus on `averages' of these data, though we also exploit over-time variation in some
27:1188:80771:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:speci\fcations. Our \frst main measure of paramilitary presence, referred to asparamilitary attacks,
27:1189:80871:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is total paramilitary attacks between 1997 and 2005 in municipalitymper 1000 inhabitants where
27:1190:80965:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the population measure is the average population between the 1993 and 2005 censuses. Our second
27:1191:81060:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f4:measure is a dummy that takes the value of 1 if municipalitymhas a value ofparamilitary attacks
27:1192:81155:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:above the 75th percentile.28We also construct two similar measures with the displaced variable
27:1193:81249:17:17:82:429:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and identical measures for guerrilla attacks (FARC and ELN combined).
27:1194:81318:17:17:99:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We take elections results from the Senate, Congress and Presidential elections 1991-2006 from
27:1195:81411:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the Registradur--a Nacional del Estado Civil. Using the names of the political parties to which
27:1196:81506:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:politicians belonged, we constructed party vote shares in each municipality. We then classi\fed
27:1197:81601:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:parties into `third', `left' and `traditional' (Liberals or Conservatives) political parties, and calcu-
27:1198:81705:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:lated the vote share of third parties in each municipality.29For Presidential elections we took the
27:1199:81804:17:18:82:299:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:numbers from the \frst round election results.
27:1200:81850:18:17:99:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In addition to the third party vote share, we also investigate the e-ect of paramilitaries on
27:1201:81943:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:electoral outcomes by looking at electoral concentration. This is motivated by the case study
27:1202:82036:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:evidence from Magdalena, which is discussed in the Appendix, which shows how paramilitary
27:1203:82125:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in\ruence creates a highly concentrated vote share pattern in a few municipalities (where they
27:1204:82219:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:have presumably used coercion or manipulated the vote).Electoral concentrationis de\fned as
27:1205:82310:17:17:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the vote share of the most popular list in a municipality (for the Senate or Congress, and in the
27:1206:82407:17:17:82:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tables it is referred to as `winning votes share').30Finally, we obtained data from two crucial
27:1207:82502:17:13:82:298:197:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:roll-call votes from theGacetas del Senado.31
27:1208:82547:13:15:91:543:184:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:28Less than half of the municipalities have any paramilitaryAttacks; in contrast, only two municipalities have
27:1209:82657:15:7:82:367:169:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:zeroDisplacements, though several municipalities have very low levels.
27:1210:82727:7:15:91:543:162:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:29Given our focus on the impact of the AUC, when we examine votes for third parties, we do not consider parties
27:1211:82838:15:11:82:543:147:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:in the left-wing coalition, the Polo Democr-atico (`Democratic pole'), which are unconnected with the paramilitaries,
27:1212:82955:11:7:82:399:136:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:as `third parties'. See Valencia (2007) for a similar distinction and calculation.
27:1213:83037:7:15:91:543:129:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:30The results using a Her\fndahl index to measure electoral concentration are very similar and omitted to save
27:1214:83147:15:7:82:106:114:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:space.
27:1215:83153:7:0:91:389:107:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:31Roll-calls are not taken for most votes in either the Senate or Congress.
28:1216:83230:0:17:99:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:As controls, we collected data on the vote share of-Alvaro G-omez in the 1986 Presidential
28:1217:83320:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:election to construct a measure of the extent of `right-wing' support in a municipality. G-omez
28:1218:83415:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:was the son of the right wing conservative President Laureano G-omez from the earlier 1950s and
28:1219:83510:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ran on a very conservative platform as the Presidential candidate for the Conservative party.
28:1220:83603:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Similarly, we use the vote share of Jaime Pardo Leal the Presidential candidate for the Uni-on
28:1221:83697:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Patri-otica in the same election. Since the Uni-on Patri-otica was the uno-cial political wing of the
28:1222:83798:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:FARC, Pardo Leal's vote share is a good measure of `left-wing' support in a municipality. In many
28:1223:83895:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of our regressions, we also include interactions between a full set of time dummies and various
28:1224:83990:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:municipality-level controls. These controls are the land Gini in 1985, the area of the municipality,
28:1225:84090:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:altitude, distance to state capital, average municipality population between 1993 and 2005, an
28:1226:84184:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:index of how rural the population of the municipality is (in 1993), an index of `unful\flled basic
28:1227:84282:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:needs' in 1993, proxying for the level of poverty in the municipality, and dummies for coca
28:1228:84373:17:30:82:541:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:cultivation in 1994 and opium cultivation in 1994 (these controls are from the CEDE database).
28:1229:84467:30:24:82:237:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:4.2  Descriptive Statistics
28:1230:84494:24:17:82:543:450:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 2 shows the descriptive statistics. Columns 1 and 2 report the mean and standard devia-
28:1231:84587:17:17:82:543:433:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tion of the variables for the whole sample. Columns 3-6 report the same two variables for high
28:1232:84681:17:17:82:543:416:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary areas where we use the attacks dummy de\fned in the last section to decide whether
28:1233:84776:17:17:82:336:399:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:or not a municipality has high paramilitary presence.
28:1234:84829:17:17:99:543:382:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The \frst two sets of rows show the rapid increase in paramilitary presence between 1996-1997
28:1235:84922:17:17:82:543:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and 2000-2001 with some evidence that this fell in 2004-2005. Interestingly, the next set of rows
28:1236:85019:17:17:82:543:348:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:show a similar increase in guerilla presence (with no tendency to fall in the most recent period,
28:1237:85116:17:17:82:543:331:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:despite President Uribe's intensi\fcation of the war against the FARC). Looking at columns 3
28:1238:85208:17:17:82:543:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and 5 it is evident that there is a positive correlation between paramilitary presence and guerilla
28:1239:85307:17:17:82:543:297:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence, which is not surprising since, as we discussed above, paramilitary units were often
28:1240:85400:17:17:82:228:280:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:formed to combat the guerilla.
28:1241:85430:17:17:99:543:263:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There are several noteworthy features of the data highlighted by Table 2. Rows 9-12 show a
28:1242:85520:17:17:82:543:246:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:large increase in the share of third parties after 2002, and this increase is more pronounced in
28:1243:85616:17:17:82:543:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:high paramilitary areas. Our measure of electoral concentration also increases after 2002, and
28:1244:85710:17:17:82:543:212:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:this is again largely concentrated in high paramilitary areas (rows 13-16). Finally, rows 17 and
28:1245:85806:17:17:82:543:195:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:18 show a noticeable increase in the vote share of the winning presidential candidate in the high
28:1246:85903:17:17:82:543:178:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary areas. These patterns give a preview of our regression evidence that will be presented
28:1247:86002:17:17:82:476:161:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the next section, as part of the evidence of paramilitary involvement in politics.
28:1248:86087:17:17:99:543:144:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Rows 19-24 show that there are also some notable di-erences between high and low paramili-
28:1249:86177:17:17:82:543:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tary areas in terms of the covariates. Most importantly, low paramilitary areas appear to be more
28:1250:86274:17:17:82:543:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:`right-wing'. This is reassuring in connection with the concerns that our measure of paramilitary
28:1251:86371:17:0:82:543:93:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence will capture latent right-wing leanings. There are also some di-erences in terms of other
29:1252:86471:0:35:82:312:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:covariates, though these appear relatively small.
29:1253:86520:35:28:82:428:673:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:5  The Impact of Non-State Actors on Elections
29:1254:86566:28:17:82:543:645:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We now investigate econometrically the impact of non-state armed actors on electoral outcomes,
29:1255:86660:17:17:82:543:628:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:starting with their impact on the vote share of third parties. Our basic regressions will be from
29:1256:86757:17:27:82:314:611:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a simple panel data model of the following form:
29:1257:86805:27:28:188:543:584:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:ym;t=dt+-m+-t-Pm+\ft-Gm+X0m;t--+"m;t;(7)
29:1258:86845:28:17:82:543:556:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whereym;tis the outcome variable in municipalitymat timet, thedt's denote time e-ects, the
29:1259:86935:17:17:82:543:539:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:-m's are municipality \fxed e-ects,Xm;tis a vector of covariates, which contains the interactions
29:1260:87032:17:17:82:543:522:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between various geographic and political controls at the municipality level (described above) and a
29:1261:87131:17:17:82:543:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:full set of time dummies that are included in some speci\fcations;"m;tis an error term representing
29:1262:87230:17:17:82:543:488:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:all omitted factors. Most importantly,Pmis our time-invariant measure of paramilitary presence
29:1263:87324:17:18:82:543:471:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:andGmas the corresponding measure of guerilla presence. The term-t-Pmtherefore estimates
29:1264:87412:18:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a potentially di-erential growth e-ect for every time period (relative to the base, initial date).
29:1265:87510:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This speci\fcation will enable us to focus on whether there is a change in an outcome variable
29:1266:87604:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(for example, the third party vote share) after the AUC become involved in politics. Our \frst
29:1267:87698:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:dependent variable will be the vote share of third parties, proxying for the direct e-ect of the
29:1268:87794:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:AUC in elections, and we have these data for the 1991, 1994, 1998, 2002 and 2006 elections.
29:1269:87885:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This enables us to include interactions with the 1994, 1998, 2002 and 2006 dummies and our
29:1270:87975:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:measures of paramilitary presence as a check against pre-existing trends (1991 election is the
29:1271:88069:17:17:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:omitted category). Our working hypothesis that the AUC in\ruenced elections and forced citizens
29:1272:88164:17:17:82:434:317:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to vote for certain lists (or used ballot stu-ng) implies-t>0 after 2002.
29:1273:88237:17:28:99:416:300:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We also experimented with empirical models of the following form
29:1274:88301:28:28:113:543:272:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:ym;t=dt+-m+-t-Pm;t-1+--Pm;t-1+\ft-Gm;t-1+--Gm;t-1+X0m;t--+"m;t;(8)
29:1275:88367:28:17:82:543:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which include both a time-varying main e-ect of paramilitary and guerrilla presence, and focus
29:1276:88461:17:17:82:543:227:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on the interaction between year e-ects and the time-varying measures. The disadvantage of this
29:1277:88555:17:17:82:543:210:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:model is that, as noted above, year-to-year variation in paramilitary and guerrilla presence is often
29:1278:88656:17:17:82:543:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:due to measurement error. To minimize the impact of year-to-year variations, we estimate (8)
29:1279:88748:17:17:82:542:176:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:only using the election years for 1998, 2002 and 2006 and construct two dummy variablesPm;t-1
29:1280:88841:17:17:82:543:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:andGm;t-1using the two years prior to the election. We then setPm;t-1= 1 if municipalitymis
29:1281:88932:17:17:82:543:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:above the 75th percentile.Gm;t-1is constructed similarly. For the 1998 election we just use the
29:1282:89027:17:17:82:543:125:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1997 data, for 2002 we used data from 2000 and 2001, and so on. Equation (8) also includes the
29:1283:89121:17:0:82:251:108:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:direct e-ects ofPm;t-1andGm;t-1.
30:1284:89155:0:24:82:394:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:5.1  Paramilitary E-ect on Elections|Third Parties
30:1285:89205:24:17:82:543:684:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We \frst investigate the impact of paramilitary presence on the vote share of third parties in the
30:1286:89303:17:17:82:543:667:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Senate elections. More speci\fcally, we estimate equations (7) and (8), with the dependent variable
30:1287:89402:17:17:82:543:650:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:ym;tcorresponding to the vote share of third parties in municipalitymin the elections for Senate
30:1288:89498:17:17:82:543:633:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:at timet. Our basic results, using theattacksmeasure, are reported in Table 3. In this and all
30:1289:89592:17:17:82:543:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:subsequent tables, all standard errors are fully robust (allowing for arbitrary serial correlation at
30:1290:89693:17:17:82:543:599:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the municipality level), and Tables 3-7 include a full set of municipality and time dummies in all
30:1291:89791:17:17:82:148:582:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:speci\fcations.
30:1292:89806:17:17:99:543:565:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 3 shows a robust positive and signi\fcant e-ect in both 2002 and 2006 of paramilitary
30:1293:89897:17:17:82:543:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence on the vote share of third parties. For example, column 1 estimates ^-2002= 20:97 with
30:1294:89992:17:17:82:543:531:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a standard error of 3.14 and a similar estimate for 2006, ^-2006= 22:10 (s.e.=3.19). Both esti-
30:1295:90087:17:17:82:543:514:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mates are highly statistically signi\fcant and quantitatively large (the magnitudes will be discussed
30:1296:90188:17:17:82:117:497:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:below).
30:1297:90195:17:17:99:543:480:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Column 2 adds our basic covariates (the land Gini in 1985, the area of the municipality,
30:1298:90283:17:17:82:543:463:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:altitude, distance to state capital, average population between 1993 and 2005, the index of rurality,
30:1299:90384:17:17:82:543:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the index of unful\flled basic needs, dummies for coca and opium cultivation, and our measures of
30:1300:90481:17:18:82:543:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:right and left leanings of the municipalities), all interacted with a full set of time dummies so as
30:1301:90581:18:17:82:543:411:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to allow for di-erential e-ects over time. To save space, we do not report the coe-cients on these
30:1302:90679:17:17:82:543:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:time interactions. The results in column 2 are similar to those in column 1, slightly smaller, though
30:1303:90780:17:17:82:543:377:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:still highly signi\fcant (15.88 for 2002 and 10.79 for 2006). In column 3, we include interactions
30:1304:90878:17:17:82:543:360:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with guerrilla presence as well as our main interactions of paramilitary presence and time. These
30:1305:90975:17:17:82:543:343:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:interactions are insigni\fcant, consistent with the hypothesis that the left-wing guerrillas have
30:1306:91072:17:17:82:341:326:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:played a much more limited role in national politics.32
30:1307:91127:17:17:99:543:309:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The next three columns re-estimate the same models of the \frst three columns but now
30:1308:91212:17:17:82:543:292:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:using the attacks dummy as the measure of paramilitary and guerilla presence. The results are
30:1309:91305:17:17:82:543:275:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:very similar to the \frst three columns. For example, in column 4, we estimate ^-2002= 13:71
30:1310:91397:17:17:82:543:258:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(s.e.=1.98) and ^-2006= 14:54 (s.e.=1.99), which are again statistically highly signi\fcant. The
30:1311:91493:17:17:82:543:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimates in columns 5 and 6 are very similar. These estimates also clearly show the quantitative
30:1312:91590:17:17:82:543:224:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:e-ects of paramilitary involvement. They imply that high paramilitary areas have, on average,
30:1313:91683:17:17:82:543:207:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:10 percentage points higher vote share for third parties after the AUC's involvement in politics.
30:1314:91780:17:17:82:543:190:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This is a very sizable e-ect, particularly in view of the fact that the average vote share of third
30:1315:91879:17:17:82:329:173:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:parties before 2001 was about 15 percent (Table 2).
30:1316:91930:17:17:99:543:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Prior to 2002, as the coe-cients ^-1994and ^-1998illustrate there is no robust positive relation-
30:1317:92027:17:17:82:543:139:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ship between paramilitary presence and third party vote share. Though both of these coe-cients
30:1318:92121:17:16:82:543:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are positive and signi\fcant in column 1, their signi\fcance vanishes when we add the covariates for
30:1319:92221:16:14:91:543:106:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:32This is not because we are focusing on the vote share of third parties. When we repeat these regressions using
30:1320:92333:14:0:82:513:92:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the vote share of the socialist coalition of parties, interactions with guerrilla presence are still insigni\fcant.
31:1321:92450:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:columns 2 and 3. In column 4 ^-1994is again positive and signi\fcant, though ^-1998is not. As with
31:1322:92548:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the attacks data in levels these coe-cients become completely insigni\fcant once the covariates
31:1323:92643:17:17:82:226:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are added in columns 5 and 6.
31:1324:92672:17:17:99:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:One concern with the results in columns 1-6 is that the change in the coe-cient of the time
31:1325:92763:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:interactions might re\rect the changing importance of paramilitaries or guerrillas in certain areas.
31:1326:92863:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our data are not ideal to investigate these issues, since the year-to-year variation in the military
31:1327:92963:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and guerrilla presence are measured with considerable error. Nevertheless, in columns 7 and 8,
31:1328:93057:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we estimate equation (8) to provide some answers to these questions. The most parsimonious
31:1329:93147:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:speci\fcation is presented in column 7. The results here are consistent with those in the \frst 6
31:1330:93244:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:columns using our time-invariant measure of paramilitary presence. The estimated coe-cients are
31:1331:93339:17:17:83:542:538:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:^-2002= 17:81 (s.e.=2.87) and ^-2006= 18:02 (s.e.=3.01), and are highly statistically signi\fcant.33
31:1332:93439:17:17:99:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 4 shows the results for the votes for the Congress. The general patterns and in fact even
31:1333:93534:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the point estimates are very similar to those in Table 3, with high paramilitary areas showing
31:1334:93628:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:about a 8 percentage points higher vote shares for third parties after the AUC's involvement in
31:1335:93723:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:politics.  Nevertheless, the results are weaker than in Table 3, and in column 6 where we use
31:1336:93816:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:the attacks dummy with the full set of covariates and guerilla presence neither ^-2002not ^-2006
31:1337:93912:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:statistically signi\fcant. Importantly, ^-1994and ^-1998are small and statistically insigni\fcant in
31:1338:94012:17:17:82:215:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:all speci\fcations in Table 4.
31:1339:94042:17:17:99:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 5 investigates the robustness of these results further (focusing on the votes for the
31:1340:94133:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Senate; the results for the Congress are similar).  In this table, all speci\fcations include the
31:1341:94230:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:time interactions with the full set of covariates introduced above, including the interactions with
31:1342:94329:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:guerrilla presence (which are reported in the table, while other covariates are again not reported
31:1343:94427:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to save space).  The \frst column again estimates (7), but uses the levels of displaced people
31:1344:94521:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:as the presence measure for both paramilitary and guerilla presence.  Now we see that, less
31:1345:94612:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:supportive of our hypothesis, the estimates for the interactions between all the time dummies
31:1346:94705:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and the displaced measure of paramilitary presence are statistically signi\fcant (though the point
31:1347:94803:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimates are di-erent because the scale of the displaced variable is di-erent). However, there
31:1348:94898:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is a large increase in the size of the coe-cient in 2002, though it halves in 2006. In column 2
31:1349:94993:17:17:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we use the dummy version of the displaced measure of paramilitary presence with results very
31:1350:95085:17:17:82:544:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:similar to those in column 1 except that now the quantitative magnitudes of ^-2002and ^-2006are
31:1351:95180:17:17:82:543:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:similar. Because we are now using a dummy variable for measuring paramilitary presence, the
31:1352:95271:17:17:82:543:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:quantitative e-ects can also be directly compared to those in Table 3. The estimates suggest that
31:1353:95368:17:17:82:543:163:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:high paramilitary areas experienced about 12 percentage points increase in the vote share of third
31:1354:95466:17:16:82:528:146:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:parties in 2002 and 2006, which is broadly consistent with the quantitative e-ects in Table 3.
31:1355:95560:16:14:91:543:130:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:33Notice that the direct e-ect of paramilitary presence is negative. We conjecture that this is because paramili-
31:1356:95673:14:11:82:543:116:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:taries appear to have had a very strong e-ect on elections in departments on the Caribbean coast, such as Magdalena,
31:1357:95789:11:11:82:543:105:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Sucre, C-orboda and C-esar. The third parties that existed prior to 2002 were not strong in these areas, hence the
31:1358:95903:11:0:82:431:94:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:negative correlation between paramilitary presence and third party vote share in 1998.
32:1359:95991:0:17:99:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In column 3 we again use the displaced measure, but now exploit the time series variation in
32:1360:96083:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the data estimating model (8). Here the estimates are imprecise and insigni\fcant, though still
32:1361:96178:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:positive. In column 4, we use a di-erent strategy and extract the principal component of the
32:1362:96270:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:attacks and displaced measures, and use this principal component as our measure of paramilitary
32:1363:96365:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence. The advantage of this strategy is that both attacks and displaced numbers are noisy,
32:1364:96459:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:thus their common component may contain more information. The results from this approach are
32:1365:96551:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:very much in line with those of Tables 3 and 4. We \fnd no impact of paramilitary presence prior
32:1366:96647:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to 2002 but a positive and highly signi\fcant one afterwards. In column 5, we use yet another
32:1367:96740:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:strategy and construct a dummy that takes the value 1 if in our data a municipality has high
32:1368:96832:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary presence according to both our attacks data and our displaced data (according to
32:1369:96925:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:this measure all areas for which we have data for displaced numbers but for which the attacks
32:1370:97018:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:data are missing receive a value of zero). We construct a similar dummy for the guerilla presence
32:1371:97115:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:measures. The results using this combined dummy are again very similar to our basic \fnding
32:1372:97206:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:though ^-1998is now statistically signi\fcant. Finally, in column 6, we estimate the model (8), but
32:1373:97305:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:now using a time-varying dummy constructed combining information from attacks and displaced
32:1374:97396:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:numbers as in column 5. In contrast to the imprecise results in column 3, the estimates now are
32:1375:97491:17:17:82:388:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:consistent with the rest of our results and are highly signi\fcant.
32:1376:97558:17:17:99:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A major concern for our empirical strategy is that paramilitary groups may be selecting into
32:1377:97650:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:speci\fc areas based on their political or ideological characteristics; paramilitary presence may be
32:1378:97750:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:capturing a trend towards third parties unrelated to the paramilitaries' involvement in politics
32:1379:97846:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(this has to be a trend, since all speci\fcations include a full set of municipality \fxed e-ects).
32:1380:97945:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:For example, there might be a trend in `conservative ideology' in certain areas, and the increased
32:1381:98043:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:vote share of third parties is a re\rection of this trend in the areas where they have situated.
32:1382:98139:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:While we cannot rule out this alternative explanation for the patterns shown in Tables 3-5, we
32:1383:98233:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:do not \fnd it very plausible. First, the speci\fcations with covariates \rexibly control for potential
32:1384:98336:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:di-erential trends in `right-wing ideology' by interacting the vote share of-Alvaro G-omez in the
32:1385:98433:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:1986 Presidential election with a full set of time dummies (as well as for potential di-erential
32:1386:98529:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:trends in `left-wing ideology'). Remarkably, this has almost no e-ect on the estimates. Second,
32:1387:98624:17:17:82:438:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the case study evidence discussed in Section 3 supports our interpretation.
32:1388:98699:17:17:99:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Overall, Tables 3-5 provide robust correlations consistent with our basic hypothesis that fol-
32:1389:98793:17:17:82:543:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:lowing the AUC's decision to become involved in politics, paramilitaries have systematically in-
32:1390:98889:17:17:82:543:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\ruenced electoral outcomes. The next two subsections provide further evidence consistent with
32:1391:98983:17:29:82:141:163:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:this pattern.
32:1392:98996:29:24:82:452:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:5.2  Results on Electoral Concentration: Senate and Congress
32:1393:99056:24:17:82:543:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Motivated by the case study evidence from Magdalena, discussed in the Appendix, we hypothesize
32:1394:99150:17:0:82:543:93:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that paramilitary involvement also translated into greaterelectoral concentration(greater vote
33:1395:99246:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:share for the winning list in the Senate and Congress elections). Table 6 investigates this issue
33:1396:99343:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:by estimating regressions similar to (7) and (8), with the dependent variable being the vote share
33:1397:99441:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the most popular list in either the Senate or the Congress in municipalitymat timet. For
33:1398:99532:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:these regressions, we again have data from 1991 to 2006. Throughout, we focus on the attacks
33:1399:99624:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:measure to save space (the results with the displaced measured are very similar and are available
33:1400:99721:17:17:82:151:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:upon request).
33:1401:99735:17:17:99:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The \frst six columns in Table 6 use data from the Senate, while the last six are for the
33:1402:99824:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Congress. Each of these sets of columns is broken down into three sets of two which use \frst the
33:1403:99921:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:attacks data in levels, then the attacks dummy for high paramilitary and guerilla presence, and
33:1404:100016:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\fnally the time varying attacks dummy. All columns include the full set of covariates (interacted
33:1405:100114:17:17:82:239:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with a full set of time dummies).
33:1406:100147:17:17:99:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This table shows no di-erential trend in electoral concentration between high and low paramil-
33:1407:100241:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:itary areas before 2002. There is also no di-erential trend at any point between high and low
33:1408:100334:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:guerrilla areas. There is a large spike in electoral concentration in 2002 in high paramilitary areas,
33:1409:100436:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which is visible in columns 1-4 and 7-10. This e-ect disappears in 2006, and is not visible or is
33:1410:100533:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:only imprecisely estimated in speci\fcations that use the time-varying measures (the regression
33:1411:100628:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:equation (8), cfr. columns 5, 6, 11 and 12). The quantitative e-ects in 2002 are large, correspond-
33:1412:100727:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ing to about a 4-5 percentage points increase in the vote share of the winning candidate (list).
33:1413:100823:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This is again a very large e-ect, as the vote share of the winning list in Senate and Congress
33:1414:100917:17:17:82:295:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:elections was around 30 percent before 2001.
33:1415:100961:17:17:99:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:An obvious question is why there is no di-erential e-ect on electoral concentration in high
33:1416:101052:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary areas in 2006. The answer to this question is suggested by our discussion of the
33:1417:101145:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:evidence from Magdalena in the Appendix and by the arguments advanced by Valencia (2007)
33:1418:101233:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and L-opez (2007): after the experience of 2002, which was subsequently highly scrutinized in
33:1419:101326:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:places such as Magdalena, paramilitaries became much more skilled at manipulating the outcomes
33:1420:101420:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in order to guarantee the election of their candidates without drawing so much attention to
33:1421:101511:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:themselves. As we show in the Appendix, even if electoral concentration fell in Magdalena in
33:1422:101603:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2006, Senators supported by the paramilitaries were re-elected and with a rather similar number
33:1423:101698:17:17:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of votes, but now spread more evenly throughout the department. Indeed, recalling the evidence
33:1424:101792:17:17:82:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Table 1, the presence in the legislature after 2006 of so many Senators and Congressmen
33:1425:101882:17:17:82:543:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:either under investigation or arrested for connections with paramilitaries is direct evidence of a
33:1426:101980:17:17:82:543:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:continuing impact of the paramilitaries on elections. This interpretation is also supported by the
33:1427:102078:17:17:82:543:163:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:evidence presented in the previous subsection (Tables 3-5), which showed the robust association
33:1428:102173:17:17:82:543:146:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between paramilitary presence and the rise of third parties in the elections of both 2002 and
33:1429:102266:17:17:82:543:129:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2006. Had the e-ect of the paramilitaries on the electoral outcomes weakened in 2006, we would
33:1430:102360:17:17:82:543:112:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:have seen this in a decline in the vote share of third parties. The results from the votes for the
33:1431:102458:17:0:82:479:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:executive, presented in the next subsection, further corroborate this interpretation.
34:1432:102545:0:24:82:262:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:5.3  Results for the Executive
34:1433:102575:24:17:82:543:684:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 7 presents estimates from regression models similar to (7) and (8) for the period 1998-2006,
34:1434:102673:17:17:82:543:667:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:withym;tde\fned as the share of votes of the winning Presidential candidate in municipalitymat
34:1435:102767:17:17:82:543:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:timet. Once again we focus on the attacks measure (the results with the displaced measure are
34:1436:102860:17:17:82:543:633:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:again very similar). The basic robust \fnding is that in both 2002 and in 2006 the vote share of the
34:1437:102960:17:17:82:543:616:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:winning candidate (-Alvaro Uribe) was systematically higher in high paramilitary areas than the
34:1438:103055:17:17:82:543:599:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:vote share of the winning candidate in 1998 (Pastrana); this e-ect is in fact considerably stronger
34:1439:103154:17:17:82:543:582:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in 2006. For example, the estimate in column 4, 11.45 (s.e. = 1.67) suggests that Uribe obtained
34:1440:103250:17:17:82:543:565:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:about 11 percentage points more votes in high paramilitary areas than Pastrana did. The same
34:1441:103342:17:17:82:543:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:e-ect is present in models that exploit the time-varying measures of paramilitary presence (models
34:1442:103440:17:17:82:129:531:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:as in (8)).
34:1443:103451:17:17:99:543:514:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The pattern with a stronger e-ect in 2006 is plausible.  President Uribe was favored by
34:1444:103538:17:17:82:543:497:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary groups already in 2002, but after his support for policies in line with these groups'
34:1445:103636:17:17:82:543:480:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:interests during his \frst term, the support of the paramilitary groups for his election became
34:1446:103731:17:17:82:543:463:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:much stronger. This pattern is thus consistent both with the notion that paramilitaries continued
34:1447:103828:17:17:82:543:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to heavily in\ruence elections after 2002, and also with the hypothesis, documented further below,
34:1448:103926:17:18:82:543:429:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that a symbiotic relationship between the executive and the paramilitaries developed after certain
34:1449:104024:18:17:82:257:411:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:key legislations proposed by Uribe.34
34:1450:104061:17:17:99:543:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The evidence in this subsection is also particularly important since it suggests that, consistent
34:1451:104158:17:17:82:543:377:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with the assumptions of our theoretical model, the executive, President Uribe, electorally bene\fted
34:1452:104258:17:29:82:260:360:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:from the presence of paramilitaries.35
34:1453:104296:29:24:82:221:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:5.4  Predicting Arrests
34:1454:104319:24:17:82:543:307:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:As noted in the Introduction, since the so called `Parapol--tica' scandal \frst broke in Colombia,
34:1455:104417:17:17:82:543:290:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:many Congressmen and Senators have been investigated, arrested for and even found guilty of links
34:1456:104514:17:17:82:543:273:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with illegal paramilitary organizations. A useful `reality check' on whether the evidence reported
34:1457:104612:17:17:82:543:256:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:so far indeed represents the in\ruence of paramilitaries on election outcomes is to see whether
34:1458:104707:17:16:82:543:239:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Senators elected in areas under paramilitary control have explicit links with the paramilitaries
34:1459:104803:16:15:91:543:223:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:34Nevertheless, as always, there may be other interpretations of this \fnding. For instance, to the extent that
34:1460:104914:15:10:82:543:208:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:President Uribe had been successful in de-mobilizing the paramilitaries, then people who had previously su-ered
34:1461:105025:10:11:82:543:198:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:under them might have rewarded the President by supporting his bid for re-election. Although we cannot rule out
34:1462:105136:11:11:82:543:187:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:this alternative explanation, the case study evidence is more consistent with our proposed interpretation and with
34:1463:105250:11:8:82:203:176:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the implications of our model.
34:1464:105280:8:14:91:543:168:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:35In May 2008, somewhat surprisingly given his insistence that paramilitary crimes should not be extraditable,
34:1465:105390:14:11:82:543:154:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:President Uribe extradited 14 paramilitary leaders, including Salvatore Mancuso, Jorge 40 and Don Berna. Our
34:1466:105498:11:11:82:543:143:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:model gives two ways to think about this. First, the more popular President Uribe is with the general population,
34:1467:105611:11:11:82:543:132:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the less he needs the paramilitaries. It may therefore not be a coincidence that the extraditions took place soon
34:1468:105724:11:11:82:543:121:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:after the killing by the military of FARC senior cadre, Ra-ul Reyes, which was hugely popular in Colombia. Second,
34:1469:105838:11:11:82:543:110:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:it is possible that the paramilitary leaders began to develop national political aspirations, which our model suggests
34:1470:105956:11:0:82:234:99:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:would make Uribe turn against them.
35:1471:105993:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and have voted for legislation favoring paramilitary interests. In this subsection, we investigate the
35:1472:106095:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence of explicit links, exploiting the fact that Colombian judiciary, particularly the Supreme
35:1473:106193:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Court, is broadly independent and has prosecuted politicians with links with the paramilitaries.
35:1474:106289:17:17:82:434:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The voting behavior of these Senators is discussed in the next subsection.
35:1475:106363:17:17:99:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We adopt a simple empirical strategy to measure the extent to which Senators relied on the
35:1476:106453:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:support of paramilitaries for their election. First, we de\fne!lPto be the proportion of total vote
35:1477:106552:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that Senate listlreceives in municipalities with high paramilitary presence, where we measure high
35:1478:106650:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary presence by using our dummy variable constructed from our time-invariant measure
35:1479:106743:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of paramilitary presence. Similarly we de\fne!lGas the proportion of total vote that listlreceives
35:1480:106841:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in municipalities with high guerilla presence, where high guerilla presence is measured in the same
35:1481:106940:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:way as paramilitary presence. To investigate the links between Senators and paramilitaries, we
35:1482:107034:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:look at Senators who are arrested for connections with paramilitary groups. We de\fne -las
35:1483:107124:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the proportion of the Senators of listlthat have been arrested for alleged connections with
35:1484:107215:17:28:82:266:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary groups and then estimate
35:1485:107252:28:27:227:543:459:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:-l=--!l;P+--!l;G+X0l--+"l:(9)
35:1486:107281:27:17:82:543:432:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Based on our hypothesis that Senators and Congressmen receiving a high fraction of their votes
35:1487:107375:17:17:82:543:415:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in paramilitary areas have explicit connections with paramilitaries, we expect to \fnd- >0. In
35:1488:107469:17:17:82:543:398:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the covariate vectorX0lwe also use party identity.  Though, in general, this is an example of
35:1489:107562:17:17:82:543:381:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:`bad control' (Angrist and Pischke, 2009, pp. 64-68), since being a member of a third party is
35:1490:107656:17:17:82:543:364:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:an outcome variable inbetween the causal variable of interest,!l;P, and the outcome variable,
35:1491:107749:17:17:82:544:347:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:-l, in this case we include it to examine whether being a member of a third party absorbs all of
35:1492:107845:17:17:82:543:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the explanatory power of!l;P(thus acting as the channel through which paramilitary presence is
35:1493:107939:17:17:82:286:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:impacting politician behavior and arrests).
35:1494:107982:17:17:99:543:296:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 8 shows the results from estimating (9).  In column 1, we look at the relationship
35:1495:108070:17:17:82:543:279:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:between arrests and party identity. As we saw above, there is a close correspondence between
35:1496:108162:17:17:82:543:262:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary presence and the rise of third parties. Column 1 con\frms this, showing that third
35:1497:108257:17:17:82:543:245:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:party Senators are signi\fcantly more likely to be arrested for links with the paramilitaries than
35:1498:108355:17:17:82:432:228:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Liberals, Conservatives and Socialists (liberals are the omitted category).
35:1499:108430:17:17:99:543:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In the next three columns, columns 2-4, we present estimates of (9) for the Senate. Column 2 is
35:1500:108525:17:17:82:543:194:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the most parsimonious speci\fcation where we regress the proportion of Senators on a list who were
35:1501:108623:17:17:82:543:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:arrested on!l;Pand!l;G. We see that ^-= 1:38 (standard error=0.42) is statistically signi\fcant
35:1502:108718:17:17:82:543:160:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:suggesting that the higher the share of its votes that a list obtained in paramilitary areas, the
35:1503:108815:17:17:82:543:143:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:greater is the proportion of Senators on the list who are arrested for links with paramilitaries. In
35:1504:108915:17:17:82:543:126:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:column 3 we add as a covariate the proportion of its vote share that the list obtained in `right-
35:1505:109012:17:17:82:543:109:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:leaning' and `left-leaning' areas.36Neither of these controls are signi\fcant in themselves and they
35:1506:109112:17:0:91:543:92:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:36We de\fne the `right-leaning' and `left-leaning' dummies again by looking at the vote shares of-Alvaro G-omez and
36:1507:109229:0:17:82:287:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:do not in\ruence the coe-cients of interest.
36:1508:109273:17:17:99:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In column 4 we then add the party dummies to investigate whether the entire e-ect of the
36:1509:109361:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries is working through third parties. The estimates show that this is not the case.
36:1510:109455:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The third party dummy is still signi\fcant, but so is the share of votes from paramilitary areas.
36:1511:109552:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This suggests that the only channel of in\ruence of paramilitaries on politicians behavior is not
36:1512:109649:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:through third party a-liation (which, in hindsight, is not surprising, since in several municipali-
36:1513:109748:17:17:82:392:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ties, paramilitaries supported liberal or conservative candidates).
36:1514:109815:17:17:99:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The next four columns report estimates of (9) for the Congress. These are broadly consistent
36:1515:109907:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with the results for the Senate; the proportion of the votes that a list won in high paramilitary
36:1516:110004:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:areas is positively correlated with the proportion of Congressmen on that list who have been
36:1517:110096:17:17:82:538:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:arrested, though the results are typically somewhat less precisely estimated and less signi\fcant.
36:1518:110194:17:17:99:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Overall, these results are important \frstly because they provide some veri\fcation that our
36:1519:110286:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:strategy for measuring the e-ects of the paramilitaries is indeed capturing what they are supposed
36:1520:110384:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to. Secondly, they also show that our \fndings so far are unlikely to be driven by some omitted
36:1521:110479:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:characteristic of municipalities (making paramilitary presence `endogenous' to voters' preferences).
36:1522:110579:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The fact that paramilitary presence is positively correlated with arrests suggests that there is
36:1523:110675:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:indeed a close relationship between paramilitaries and politicians such that paramilitary groups are
36:1524:110775:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:either forming a coalition with local politicians, or are themselves running as candidates. In either
36:1525:110876:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:case, it seems highly unlikely that politicians, particularly politicians elected in high paramilitary
36:1526:110978:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:areas, are perfect agents of voters, supporting policies in line with their interests.  Instead, it
36:1527:111077:17:30:82:520:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:seems that these politicians are pursuing policies systematically preferred by paramilitaries.
36:1528:111171:30:24:82:234:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:5.5  Voting in the Senate
36:1529:111196:24:17:82:543:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:As a \fnal demonstration of the potential in\ruence of the paramilitaries on elections, we examine
36:1530:111294:17:17:82:543:297:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whether Senators from lists that received large shares of their votes in paramilitary areas vote in
36:1531:111393:17:17:82:543:280:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:systematically di-erent ways. We do this in the very speci\fc but revealing context of a roll-call
36:1532:111491:17:17:82:543:263:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:vote to re-introduce two clauses of the Justice and Peace Law.  These were Article 70, which
36:1533:111583:17:17:82:543:246:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:stipulated a 10% reduction in the sentences of demobilized paramilitaries who had been charged
36:1534:111677:17:17:82:543:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:at the time of the passing of the law and Article 71, which speci\fed that the crimes of former
36:1535:111772:17:17:82:543:212:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries should be considered as `sedition'.37The main signi\fcance of sedition is that it
36:1536:111868:17:17:82:543:195:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:would imply that the paramilitaries had committed political crimes and would therefore not be
36:1537:111961:17:20:82:543:178:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:eligible to extradition.38These two articles were part of a \frst draft of the law presented by the
36:1538:112060:20:11:82:543:158:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Jaime Pardo Leal in 1986; then, similar to the construction of the dummies for paramilitary and guerrilla presence,
36:1539:112175:11:10:82:543:147:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:we constructed dummy variables for `right-leaning' and `left-leaning' areas depending on whether a municipality is
36:1540:112289:10:8:82:487:137:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:above the 75th percentile of votes for the corresponding candidate in the 1986 presidential elections.
36:1541:112391:8:14:91:543:129:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:37At the time of the votes these clauses were actually Article 61 (sentence reduction) and Article 64 (sedition)
36:1542:112503:14:8:82:216:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:but this changed in the \fnal law.
36:1543:112537:8:14:91:543:107:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:38This is a topic with a long and contested history in Colombia. During the writing of the 1991 Constitution,
36:1544:112646:14:0:82:543:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Pablo Escobar systematically tried to intimidate delegates in order to make sure that the new Constitution made
37:1545:112759:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:President but they were both rejected in the \frst commissions of the Senate and the Congress.
37:1546:112853:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The rejection of these two articles was then appealed in the Senate. In response to this appeal
37:1547:112948:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a commission was formed to inform the Senate on how to proceed with the appeal pleading.
37:1548:113036:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The members of the commission were Mario Uribe (under arrest in 2008 for connections with
37:1549:113125:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitaries and a cousin of President Uribe), Mauricio Pimiento (arrested and found guilty,
37:1550:113219:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:see Table 1), Juan G-omez, Miguel de la Espriella (arrested and found guilty, see Table A1), Jes-us
37:1551:113318:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Carrizosa, and Hernando Escobar. The members of the commission concluded that the appeal
37:1552:113406:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:had to be approved by the plenary of the Senate which it was and we have the roll-call for this
37:1553:113501:17:17:82:542:572:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:vote. This vote went in favor of re-introducing the two articles into the Justice and Peace law.39
37:1554:113599:17:17:99:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To the extent that there is a positive correlation between the proportion of votes a list received
37:1555:113697:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in paramilitary areas and the proportion of Senators on the list who voted to re-introduce these
37:1556:113793:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:two articles, this would be further evidence that paramilitaries have indeed in\ruenced election
37:1557:113889:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:outcomes, consistent with Proposition 2 of our model. Implicitly, it is also evidence of the `quid
37:1558:113987:17:17:82:478:487:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:pro quo' between paramilitaries and the executive, consistent with Proposition 4.40
37:1559:114070:17:17:99:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To examine the impact of the paramilitaries on these roll-call votes, we estimate versions of
37:1560:114163:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:model (9) in the previous sub-section. More speci\fcally we now de\fne -lto be the proportion of
37:1561:114259:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Senators on listlthat voted in favor of re-introducing these two clauses. The results are reported
37:1562:114357:17:17:82:212:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in columns 9-12 of Table 8.
37:1563:114384:17:17:99:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Column 9 shows that senators from third parties and the conservatives are most likely to
37:1564:114472:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:support the re-introduction of the two controversial articles of the Justice and Peace Law. The
37:1565:114567:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:fact that conservatives were as likely as third party candidates to support these clauses is probably
37:1566:114668:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:related to the fact that in the Senate they were also allied with President Uribe. The remaining
37:1567:114764:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:columns show a positive signi\fcant correlation between paramilitary presence in areas where a list
37:1568:114863:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:got a large proportion of its votes and the proportion of Senators who voted in favor of making
37:1569:114958:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the Peace and Justice Law more `pro-paramilitary'. (This e-ect is no longer signi\fcant in column
37:1570:115055:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:12 when we introduce the party identity variables, suggesting that a large part of the e-ect is
37:1571:115150:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:working through third party a-liation). Third party identity is again positive and signi\fcant.
37:1572:115245:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Note also that in none of the speci\fcations is there any e-ect of guerilla presence or right or left
37:1573:115346:17:17:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:orientation on these votes. Overall, we interpret this as evidence in support of our hypothesis
37:1574:115441:17:17:82:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that politicians receiving support from paramilitaries have in turn supported legislation in line
37:1575:115538:17:19:82:244:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with the interests of these groups.
37:1576:115573:19:11:82:543:178:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:extradition unconstitutional. The day after this was written into the Constitution, Pablo Escobar, who had been
37:1577:115684:11:11:82:543:167:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:in hiding, gave himself up to the authorities.  However, the Constitution was subsequently amended to allow
37:1578:115791:11:7:82:129:156:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:extradition.
37:1579:115803:7:15:91:543:149:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:39However the Supreme Court said that paramilitaries cannot be considered as seditious. So article 71 is currently
37:1580:115917:15:11:82:543:134:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:not being applied. Interestingly, even though President Uribe supported this clause, he then extradited 14 of the
37:1581:116030:11:7:82:259:123:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:paramilitary leaders as we discussed earlier.
37:1582:116075:7:15:91:543:116:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:40As we discussed in Section 3, a large literature has heavily criticized the Justice and Peace Law as being very
37:1583:116188:15:11:82:543:101:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:weak and not forcing ex-combatants to account for their crimes or provide any sort of compensation for their
37:1584:116296:11:0:82:320:90:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:victims. The structure of the law came from the executive.
38:1585:116356:0:28:82:369:708:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:6  The Persistence of the Paramilitaries
38:1586:116396:28:17:82:543:680:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Having provided some evidence consistent with the assumption that paramilitaries have had
38:1587:116485:17:17:82:543:663:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:systematic e-ects on elections in Colombia, we now turn to two predictions of our theoretical
38:1588:116578:17:17:82:543:646:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:model.  First, the model suggests that to the extent that paramilitaries deliver votes to the
38:1589:116671:17:17:82:543:629:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:President, the President will have a greater incentive to allow them to stay in control of the areas
38:1590:116771:17:17:82:543:612:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:where they are. Second, this e-ect will be stronger in places which President Uribe did not expect
38:1591:116869:17:17:82:336:595:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to do well without intervention by the paramilitaries.
38:1592:116923:17:17:99:543:578:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We focus on the 2002 Presidential election and the subsequent persistence of paramilitaries.
38:1593:117015:17:17:82:543:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We restrict attention to only municipalities that had paramilitary presence in 2000-2001.  A
38:1594:117107:17:17:82:543:544:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:municipality is classi\fed as having paramilitary presence if it experienced any paramilitary related
38:1595:117208:17:17:82:543:527:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:incidents (attacks or displacement depending on the measure used) during either 2000 or 2001.
38:1596:117301:17:17:82:543:510:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We use a time varying measure of paramilitary presence to capture presence before the election,
38:1597:117396:17:17:82:543:493:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:denotedPm;t<2002, and presence after the election, denotedPm;t>2002. In our baseline speci\fcation
38:1598:117494:17:17:82:543:476:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:this is measured as the sum of either attacks or displacements during a two-year window, the
38:1599:117586:17:17:82:543:459:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:periods 2000 and 2001 (t<2002) or between 2004 and 2005 (t>2002) in either case divided by
38:1600:117676:17:17:82:543:442:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the population of the municipality. Our results are robust to di-erent ways of measuring these
38:1601:117770:17:17:82:543:425:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:variables as we show.  We can use this variable to explicitly examine how the persistence of
38:1602:117862:17:17:82:543:408:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary presence depends on the extent of voting for President Uribe, thus testing the \frst
38:1603:117959:17:17:82:543:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:prediction. To test the second implication of the model we argue that even though when Uribe
38:1604:118051:17:17:82:543:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:was Governor of Antioquia he was nominally a representative of the Liberal Party, in fact his key
38:1605:118148:17:17:82:543:357:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:supporters, in the absence of coercion, were conservative voters who liked his emphasis on law
38:1606:118242:17:17:82:543:340:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and order. Direct evidence comes from the fact that the Conservative Party chose not to run
38:1607:118333:17:17:82:543:323:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:a candidate against him either in 2002 or 2006, while the Liberal Party did (Horacio Serpa in
38:1608:118426:17:17:82:543:306:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:both cases). As a consequence, Uribe could anticipate doing well in places where Conservative
38:1609:118519:17:17:82:543:289:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:President Andr-es Pastrana had received a high vote share in 1998. We can therefore test the
38:1610:118611:17:17:82:499:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:second hypothesis by interacting Pastrana's vote share in 1998 with Uribe's vote share.
38:1611:118698:17:28:99:329:255:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:More formally, we estimate the following model:
38:1612:118745:28:28:98:543:227:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:Pm;t>2002=--Pm;t<2002+\f-vum;2002+\r-vum;2002-vpm;1998+--vpm;1998+X0m--+"m(10)
38:1613:118823:28:17:82:543:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:wherevum;2002is the vote share of President Uribe in municipalitymin 2002 andvpm;1998is the vote
38:1614:118919:17:17:82:543:182:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:share of Pastrana in 1998. Our model predicts that\f >0 (a greater share of votes for Uribe would
38:1615:119016:17:17:82:543:165:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:lead to greater paramilitary presence after 2002), and\r <0|so that the higher was Pastrana's
38:1616:119109:17:17:82:543:148:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:vote share in 1998, the less Uribe would bene\ft from the support of the paramilitaries and thus
38:1617:119205:17:17:82:515:131:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:according to our theoretical model, the more likely are the paramilitaries to be eliminated.
38:1618:119297:17:17:99:543:114:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:An alternative measure of the paramilitary-induced vote advantage of Uribe, which is more
38:1619:119386:17:0:82:543:97:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:closely related to the predictions of Proposition 3, is to de\fne the variable maxf0; vum;2002-vpm;1998g,
39:1620:119493:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which directly captures the vote advantage of Uribe in 2002 relative to Pastrana's vote in 1998,
39:1621:119589:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:if any (in municipalitym). With the same reasoning, we expect the coe-cient on this variable to
39:1622:119684:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:be positive|the greater isvum;2002-vpm;1998, the more Uribe gained relative to Pastrana and the
39:1623:119779:17:17:82:309:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:more we would expect paramilitaries to persist.
39:1624:119826:17:17:99:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The results from estimating various versions of (10) are shown in Table 9. Throughout this
39:1625:119916:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:table and the next where we examine robustness, all of the main e-ects are evaluated at the sample
39:1626:120014:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:means to facilitate interpretation. The \frst six columns of Table 9 use theattacksmeasure non-
39:1627:120109:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:state armed actor presence, while the next four use thedisplacedmeasure. The \fnal two use the
39:1628:120203:17:17:82:324:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\frst principal component of attacks and displaced.
39:1629:120254:17:17:99:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The results are broadly consistent with our model, in particular, with the predictions of
39:1630:120343:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Proposition 3.  In column 1 of Table 9 we estimate the simplest version of (10).  Consistent
39:1631:120435:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:with these predictions, the estimate of Uribe's vote share of value to the sample mean,\f, is
39:1632:120528:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:estimated at 0:14 (with a standard error=0.08). This estimate, which is marginally signi\fcant,
39:1633:120623:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:suggests that other things equal, the greater the vote share for President Uribe in the 2002
39:1634:120715:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:election in municipalitym, the greater the paramilitary presence in the municipality after 2002.
39:1635:120811:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Quantitatively this is a sizable, though not implausible, e-ect implying that a 10% increase in
39:1636:120906:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Uribe's vote share in an average municipality under paramilitary control will increase paramilitary
39:1637:121005:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence by 0.014. This is a large e-ect compared to the mean of paramilitary presence in the
39:1638:121098:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:whole sample, which is 0.04, though smaller for the mean when we restrict attention to only those
39:1639:121195:17:17:82:435:385:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:municipalities which had positive paramilitary presence, this being 0.15.41
39:1640:121270:17:17:99:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Moreover, again consistent with the predictions of Proposition 3, the coe-cient on the in-
39:1641:121360:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:teraction between Uribe's and Pastrana's vote shares is negative and statistically signi\fcant at
39:1642:121457:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:5%, ^\r=-0:63 (standard error=0.33). This implies that, all else equal, paramilitaries were more
39:1643:121553:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:likely to persist in areas where President Uribe received a high share of votes,andon the basis
39:1644:121648:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the votes of President Pastrana in the 1998 election, he would have been expected to receive a
39:1645:121745:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:lower vote share. Column 2 adds covariates to the basic model of Column 1 while Column 3 adds
39:1646:121838:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:controls for guerilla presence in 2000-2001. In these columns, the interaction term remains nega-
39:1647:121935:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tive and has a similar quantitative magnitudes to that in Column 1, but is no longer statistically
39:1648:122033:17:17:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:signi\fcant (in several other speci\fcations in this and the next table, the interaction term is again
39:1649:122135:17:17:82:138:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:signi\fcant).
39:1650:122148:17:17:99:543:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Column 4 reports a regression model more directly inspired by Proposition 3, which makes the
39:1651:122240:17:17:82:543:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:persistence of paramilitaries a function of the vote gain of President Uribe relative to President

39:1653:122438:17:17:82:502:146:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in column 3 (coe-cient = 0.25, s.e. = 0.15), consistent with our theoretical predictions.
39:1654:122527:17:16:99:543:129:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In Columns 5 and 6, we use the logarithms of all of the variables so we lose a lot of observa-
39:1655:122621:16:14:91:543:113:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:41Since this is the e-ect at the sample mean and\r<0, the impact of Uribe's vote share is signi\fcantly higher
39:1656:122731:14:0:82:259:99:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:in municipalities with lower Pastrana share.
40:1657:122777:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tions (all the zeros). In Column 5 with this speci\fcation the direct e-ect of Uribe's vote share

40:1659:122973:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:also includes guerrilla presence before 2002 as in Column 3). In Column 6, the coe-cient on
40:1660:123064:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:maxf0; vum;2002-vpm;1998gis again positive and marginally signi\fcant (coe-cient = 0.56, standard
40:1661:123161:17:17:82:148:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:error = 0.30).
40:1662:123175:17:17:99:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The next four columns examine the same models using the displaced measure of paramilitary
40:1663:123264:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and guerilla presence. In all of these speci\fcations the direct e-ect of Uribe's vote share is positive

40:1666:123560:17:17:82:381:555:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:vpm;1998g, the estimated e-ect is positive and highly signi\fcant.

40:1668:123715:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:results are similar, and in fact more supportive of the predictions of our model. The direct e-ect
40:1669:123813:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Uribe's vote share evaluated at the sample mean is positive and statistically signi\fcant, and the
