40:1671:124014:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the results are now much more precisely estimated and the coe-cient on this table is now highly
40:1672:124109:17:17:82:133:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:signi\fcant.
40:1673:124121:17:17:99:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 10 investigates the robustness of the basic results in Table 9. In particular, it uses a
40:1674:124215:17:17:82:544:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:two-year window instead of the three-year window in Table 9 (that is, we de\fnePm;t<2002and
40:1675:124306:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:Pm;t>2002using 1999, 2000 and 2001 (t<2002) or between 2003, 2004, 2005 (t>2002) in either
40:1676:124396:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:case divided by the population of the municipality). The results are broadly similar to those in
40:1677:124492:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 9. In particular, the interaction term is now more precisely estimated and is statistically
40:1678:124589:17:17:82:263:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:signi\fcant in almost all speci\fcations.
40:1679:124630:17:18:99:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Overall, we interpret the results in this section as providing some support to our Proposition
40:1680:124724:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:3 that incumbent politicians in power will tend to refrain from eliminating paramilitaries in areas
40:1681:124823:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:where these groups deliver votes and that this e-ect is stronger where they would not have
40:1682:124913:17:34:82:192:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:otherwise done as well.
40:1683:124936:34:18:82:543:248:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:7  The Symbiotic Relationship between the Paramilitaries and
40:1684:124996:18:25:107:204:230:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:the Executive
40:1685:125009:25:24:82:243:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:7.1  Econometric Evidence
40:1686:125034:24:17:82:543:181:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The last section provided some evidence on a possible symbiotic relationship between the paramil-
40:1687:125131:17:17:82:543:164:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:itaries and the executive. In places where the paramilitaries delivered votes in 2002, they were
40:1688:125227:17:17:82:543:147:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:more likely to survive. To investigate this symbiotic relationship, or the `quid pro quo,' more
40:1689:125322:17:17:82:543:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:extensively, it is useful to study key legislation the executive brought to the legislature, and how
40:1690:125422:17:17:82:543:113:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary presence may have in\ruenced voting on these legislations. We can only examine the
40:1691:125517:17:0:82:543:96:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\frst issue, what laws the executive proposed, using case study evidence. To look at the second
41:1692:125614:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:issue, how paramilitary presence may have in\ruenced voting patterns, we again examine roll-call
41:1693:125710:17:17:82:109:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:votes.
41:1694:125716:17:17:99:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We focus on a very salient and relevant roll-call for which we have data: the vote on whether or
41:1695:125812:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:not to change the Constitution to drop the single-period term limit on the President. If Senators
41:1696:125909:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:who were elected with support from paramilitaries were more inclined to support this change
41:1697:126000:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the Constitution, then this would be direct, though naturally not de\fnitive, evidence that
41:1698:126094:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the paramilitaries supported Uribe either as quid pro quo or because he would naturally choose
41:1699:126188:17:17:82:352:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:policies more in line with their interests and preferences.
41:1700:126247:17:17:99:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:As in our previous analysis of roll-call votes we use a simple empirical strategy based on
41:1701:126337:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:equation (9) in subsections 5.4 and 5.5. We now de\fne -lto be the proportion of Senators on list
41:1702:126434:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:lthat voted in favor of changing the Constitution to allow President Uribe to run for re-election.
41:1703:126532:17:17:82:329:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:All of the remaining variables are de\fned as before.
41:1704:126585:17:17:99:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Table 11 looks at the roll-call vote for re-election. The structure of this table is similar to that
41:1705:126685:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Table 8, except that the two parts of the table now use the attacks and displaced measures. The
41:1706:126783:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\frst column again estimates a simple regression of -lon party dummies. It shows that members
41:1707:126876:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of third parties tended to vote in favor of re-election, as did Conservatives, while members of Left
41:1708:126976:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:parties tended to vote against (all relative to Liberals). Columns 2-4 then use the simple model
41:1709:127072:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(9) with the attacks data, while 5-7 estimate the same model using the displaced data. Using
41:1710:127164:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:either strategy, and even holding party a-liation constant, there is a robust positive e-ect of the
41:1711:127263:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:presence of paramilitaries in areas where Senate lists received a high vote share on the propensity
41:1712:127362:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of Senators on the list to vote in favor of changing the Constitution to allow President Uribe to
41:1713:127459:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:run again. This e-ect is statistically signi\fcant in all columns, except in column 7 where we also
41:1714:127558:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:include party identity (this suggests that in this instance most of the e-ects of paramilitaries on
41:1715:127657:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:politicians behavior might be working through third party a-liation). These columns also again
41:1716:127751:17:17:82:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:show that there is no robust impact of the presence of guerillas on the voting behavior of Senators
41:1717:127850:17:29:82:160:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:on this measure.
41:1718:127866:29:24:82:237:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:7.2  Case Study Evidence
41:1719:127890:24:17:82:543:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:There is a large case study literature which is consistent with the notion of a quid pro quo between
41:1720:127990:17:17:82:543:212:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:executive and paramilitary politicians. One obvious arena is the formulation of the Justice and
41:1721:128085:17:17:82:543:195:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Peace Law which took place after the secret negotiations at Santa F-e de Ralito. This law was
41:1722:128178:17:17:82:525:178:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:widely criticized both inside and outside Colombia as being far too lenient on paramilitaries.
41:1723:128272:17:17:99:543:161:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Here we focus on a very revealing more recent series of events which also seem to speak to
41:1724:128362:17:17:82:543:144:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the symbiotic relationship. Even though many Congressmen and Senators have been arrested,
41:1725:128451:17:17:82:543:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:they are replaced in the legislature by their alternates (in Spanish `suplentes') who appear on the
41:1726:128550:17:17:82:543:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:same list at the time of the election. In consequence, their political in\ruence is little diminished.
41:1727:128652:17:0:82:543:93:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:To change this situation members of Congress proposed a political reform in 2008 to remove
42:1728:128744:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:these politicians and their alternates from the legislature. This initiative was killed when many
42:1729:128841:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:politicians failed to appear for a debate so that a quorum was not reached. The fact that Senators
42:1730:128939:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:failed to appear for the vote was widely blamed on President Uribe (see the remarks of Senators
42:1731:129034:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f4:Gustavo Petro and Rafael Pardo (\Entierro de quinta"Semana, June 7, 2008),42andSemana
42:1732:129119:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:notes \If Uribismo lost its majorities in Congress, it would be di-cult to get the approval of key
42:1733:129217:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:projects, such as a new reform to that `little article' of the Constitution."43The `little article'
42:1734:129316:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(used sarcastically) in the Constitution is the change to allow President Uribe to run for a third
42:1735:129414:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:term of o-ce. This experience shows how President Uribe relies on the legislative support of
42:1736:129506:17:17:82:422:572:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:politicians deeply implicated with the paramilitaries to pass key bills.44
42:1737:129580:17:17:99:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:After this project failed the executive proposed an alternative political reform in August 2008
42:1738:129675:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:which involved changing the Constitution to take away the power of the Supreme Court to try
42:1739:129766:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Congressmen. As Jos-e Miguel Vivanco, Americas director at Human Rights Watch put it \Uribe
42:1740:129857:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is brazenly trying to take the power to investigate Congressmen away from the one institution
42:1741:129950:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that has done the most to uncover and break paramilitary in\ruence in the Congress ...  This
42:1742:130042:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:proposal serves no real purpose, other than to help members of Uribe's coalition get o- the hook"
42:1743:130139:17:35:82:226:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:(Human Rights Watch, 2008).
42:1744:130166:35:28:82:190:418:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:8  Conclusions
42:1745:130180:28:17:82:543:390:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Why are many states in less-developed societies unable to establish Weber's famous monopoly of
42:1746:130274:17:17:82:543:373:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:violence in their territories? The standard explanation relies on the inability of the central state to
42:1747:130377:17:17:82:543:356:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:broadcast its power throughout the territories that it nominally controls and views an extension
42:1748:130473:17:17:82:543:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of this power to the periphery as a natural by-product of `political modernization'. In this paper
42:1749:130571:17:17:82:543:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:we developed an alternative perspective, suggesting that the central state can develop (even
42:1750:130663:17:17:82:543:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:`modernize') without establishing such a monopoly of violence because there may be a symbiotic
42:1751:130757:17:17:82:543:288:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:relationship between the parties controlling the central state and non-state actors exercising power
42:1752:130857:17:17:82:543:271:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the peripheries of the country. The origins of this symbiotic relationship is that non-state armed
42:1753:130958:17:17:82:543:254:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:actors can provide support to those controlling the central state. This is particularly important
42:1754:131055:17:17:82:543:237:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in democracies where non-state armed actors can control elections. Since they naturally have
42:1755:131147:17:17:82:543:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:political preferences, they can (credibly) deliver votes for the national politicians in line with
42:1756:131245:17:17:82:543:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:their ideological and policy biases. Politicians elected with the implicit support of these non-state
42:1757:131346:17:17:82:543:186:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:actors will then have less incentive to eliminate them, leading to an equilibrium without a full
42:1758:131442:17:16:82:543:169:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:monopoly of violence of the central state.  We developed this idea theoretically and provided
42:1759:131535:16:11:91:381:153:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:42http://www.semana.com/noticias-nacion/entierro-quinta/112489.aspx
42:1760:131602:11:14:91:543:142:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:43In Spanish \Si el uribismo perd--a sus mayorias en el Congreso, se le har--a di\fcil lograr el visto bueno para
42:1761:131715:14:8:82:498:128:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:proyectos clave, como una nueva reforma a ese `articulito' de la Constituci-on" (Semana, June 7, 2008).
42:1762:131818:8:14:91:543:120:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:44In September 2009 both houses of the legislature voted to hold a national referendum on whether to allow Uribe
42:1763:131930:14:11:82:543:106:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:to run for a third term. Socialists and members of the Liberal party abstained in these votes so we do not have
42:1764:132041:11:0:82:202:95:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:further roll-calls on this issue.
43:1765:132076:0:17:82:380:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:empirical support using recent political events from Colombia.
43:1766:132138:17:17:99:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Our model makes a series of predictions, which we investigated using Colombian data. Our
43:1767:132226:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:empirical evidence began by using a variety of strategies to con\frm that paramilitaries have
43:1768:132319:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:indeed had a signi\fcant impact on elections in Colombia. Following the foundation of the AUC,
43:1769:132413:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:there is a sharp increase in the vote share of third parties, which were explicitly or implicitly
43:1770:132510:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:associated with paramilitaries, in areas that have high paramilitary presence. The same areas
43:1771:132603:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:also showed an increase in electoral concentration (the vote share of the most `popular' list in a
43:1772:132701:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:municipality). We also presented evidence that high paramilitary presence in areas where senators
43:1773:132798:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:received large proportions of their votes predicts how they voted on key clauses of the Justice and
43:1774:132897:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Peace Law, and whether they get arrested for illicit links with the paramilitaries. We also found
43:1775:132994:17:15:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that paramilitary presence is correlated with vote share of the winning presidential candidate,
43:1776:133089:15:19:84:147:523:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:-Alvaro Uribe.
43:1777:133103:19:17:99:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The two key predictions of our theoretical model are that paramilitaries should persist to the
43:1778:133197:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:extent that they deliver votes to politicians whose preferences are closer to their own and that this
43:1779:133298:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:e-ect is larger in areas where these politicians would otherwise not do well. These results illustrate
43:1780:133400:17:17:82:543:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the possible presence of a symbiotic relationship between the executive and the paramilitaries.
43:1781:133495:17:17:82:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:We further illustrated this relationship by showing that the proportion of the votes which a senate
43:1782:133594:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:list won in paramilitary areas is positively correlated with the proportion of Senators on the list
43:1783:133693:17:17:82:507:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that voted to change the Constitution to allow President Uribe to run for a second term.
43:1784:133781:17:17:99:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Nevertheless, neither our results nor the case study literature suggests the presence of a formal
43:1785:133878:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:`coalition' between paramilitary groups and President Uribe. They are consistent, however, with
43:1786:133973:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the idea that Uribe's policies are closer to those preferred by paramilitaries than those of other
43:1787:134071:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:parties which naturally gives the paramilitaries an interest in generating support for him. As
43:1788:134165:18:17:82:543:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Jairo Angarita former leader of the AUC's Sin-u and San Jorge blocs and Salvatore Mancuso's
43:1789:134256:17:28:82:396:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:deputy declared in September 2005, he was proud to work for the
43:1790:134319:28:29:126:382:271:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:\reelection of the best President we have ever had".45
43:1791:134373:29:17:99:543:242:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Naturally, di-erent interpretations of the data are possible. For instance, it is possible that
43:1792:134468:17:17:82:543:225:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:people in paramilitary areas are naturally pro `law and order' or more `conservative' so that pres-
43:1793:134567:17:17:82:543:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ence of paramilitaries is endogenous to `voter preferences'. If this were true our results connecting
43:1794:134668:17:17:82:543:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the presence of paramilitaries to Presidential vote share could be due to omitted variable bias.
43:1795:134764:17:17:82:543:174:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:This might also undermine our interpretation of the roll-call votes since it would imply that Sen-
43:1796:134862:17:17:82:543:157:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ators who voted to change the Constitution to allow President Uribe to run again did so because
43:1797:134957:17:17:82:543:140:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:their voters' preferred it. These alternative hypotheses do not appear plausible explanations for
43:1798:135054:17:16:82:543:123:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the patterns, however. First, our identi\fcation comes from the timing of the formation of the AUC
43:1799:135152:16:0:91:223:107:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:45El Tiempo, September 7, 2005.
44:1800:135185:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:and their decision to develop an electoral strategy (relying on intimidation, murder and manipu-
44:1801:135281:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:lation to get their candidates elected to national o-ce). For example, prior to these events, there
44:1802:135380:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:was no signi\fcant di-erences between electoral concentration in areas with or without paramili-
44:1803:135476:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:taries, indicating that political preferences did not systematically di-er between these two areas.
44:1804:135575:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:The timing of the formation of the AUC stems mostly from the collapse of the Medell--n and
44:1805:135665:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Cali drug cartels and is unlikely to re\rect a change in political preferences on the part of voters.
44:1806:135766:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Second, to the extent that voter preferences di-er with some areas being more conservative than
44:1807:135861:17:17:82:543:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:others, this would be controlled for by our use of \fxed e-ects as long as these di-erences are
44:1808:135956:17:17:82:543:572:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:time-invariant. Moreover, the case study literature suggests something of a `reality check' on this
44:1809:136055:17:17:82:543:555:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:argument since it provides extensive evidence of coercion and manipulation of elections in depart-
44:1810:136153:17:17:82:543:538:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:ments such as Magdalena, C-esar, C-orboda and Sucre with high paramilitary presence. Third, the
44:1811:136248:17:17:82:543:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:fact that paramilitary presence predicts arrests of Senators makes it improbable that politicians
44:1812:136345:17:17:82:543:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:are simply representing voter preferences. These results, along with the case study literature,
44:1813:136440:17:17:82:543:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:suggests that politicians formed coalitions with paramilitaries, or paramilitaries generated their
44:1814:136538:17:17:82:543:470:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:own politicians. Fourth, we tried to explicitly control for the time varying e-ects of conservative
44:1815:136637:17:17:82:242:453:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:leanings of certain municipalities.
44:1816:136672:17:17:99:543:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:An important area for future investigation is the impact of non-state armed actors on public
44:1817:136764:17:17:82:543:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:good provision. If the paramilitaries, for example, are e-ectively the local state, how do they do
44:1818:136862:17:17:82:543:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:at providing public goods or services relative to the legitimate state? The case study evidence
44:1819:136957:17:17:82:543:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:is mixed on this. Some, such as Guti-errez San--n and Bar-on (2005, p. 13) argue in their study
44:1820:137052:17:17:82:543:368:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of the development of the paramilitaries in Puerto Boyac-a that they undertook \investments in
44:1821:137146:17:17:82:543:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:patronage (drug stores, clinics, health campaigns, educational services)." Duncan's (2007) also
44:1822:137241:17:18:82:543:334:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:supports this idea (see also the|probably not entirely credible|claims in Casta~no, 2001). Yet
44:1823:137335:18:17:82:467:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:other anecdotes mitigate against it in Casanare, for example, and in La Guajira.
44:1824:137415:17:17:99:543:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A \fnal and crucial question concerns the external validity of these \fndings. Are the mecha-
44:1825:137508:17:17:82:543:282:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:nisms we discuss only relevant in Colombia, or do they also in\ruence the creation of the monopoly
44:1826:137606:17:17:82:543:265:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:of violence in other states? Although our arguments in this paper contrast with the emphasis of
44:1827:137701:17:17:82:543:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:much of the existing literature on state formation, there are several other instances where non-
44:1828:137797:17:17:82:543:231:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:state actors appear to play a similar role to that of paramilitaries in Colombia. For example, as
44:1829:137894:17:17:82:543:214:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:mentioned in the Introduction, the existence of the tribal areas in Waziristan does not imply that
44:1830:137992:17:17:82:543:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the state has not formed in Pakistan, but is indicative of a di-erent equilibrium pattern similar
44:1831:138089:17:17:82:543:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to that in Colombia. A related example comes from Italy and the role of the Ma\fa in delivering
44:1832:138184:17:17:82:543:163:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:votes to the Christian Democratic Party (Walston, 1988). Finally, the long autonomy of the US
44:1833:138277:17:17:82:543:146:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:South after the Hayes-Tilden agreement of 1877 until the Civil Rights and Voting Rights acts of
44:1834:138372:17:17:82:543:129:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the 1960s also presents many parallels with the Colombian case. Southern political elites were
44:1835:138466:17:17:82:543:112:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:able to establish a one-party undemocratic political system based on the disenfranchisement and
44:1836:138561:17:0:82:543:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:coercion of blacks. The power thus consolidated gave them great in\ruence in national political
45:1837:138658:0:17:82:543:708:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:institutions where they could both impede legislation they did not like, but where they also sup-
45:1838:138755:17:17:82:543:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:plied votes, which was exactly what the Hayes-Tilden deal was about. A telling piece of evidence
45:1839:138851:17:17:82:543:674:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in favor of this interpretation is provided by Franklin D. Roosevelt's reaction to a proposal to
45:1840:138947:17:17:82:543:657:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:pass legislation to attempt to restrict lynching. In response he argued that Southern legislators
45:1841:139044:17:17:82:543:640:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\are chairmen or occupy strategic places on most of the Senate and House committees ... If I
45:1842:139136:17:17:82:543:623:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:come out for the anti-lynching bill now, they will block every bill I ask Congress to pass" (quoted
45:1843:139235:17:17:82:543:606:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in Frederickson, 2001, p. 20). There is therefore some evidence that the mechanisms we have
45:1844:139326:17:0:82:310:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:identi\fed here are of quite general applicability.

51:1996:149597:0:29:183:442:708:14:g_d0_f23:14:g_d0_f23:Appendix:  The Evidence from Magdalena
51:1997:149635:29:17:99:543:679:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In this Appendix, we examine voting patterns in the Department of Magdalena, where various
51:1998:149725:17:17:82:543:662:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:paramilitary groups have been very active over our period of investigation. In Map 3 we reproduce
51:1999:149822:17:17:82:543:645:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the data on electoral concentration, de\fned as the vote share of the list that won the most votes,
51:2000:149921:17:17:82:543:628:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in Magdalena for the 1998, 2002 and 2006 elections for the Senate. We also place on the map
51:2001:150012:17:17:82:543:611:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:the proportion of votes that Senator Luis Eduardo Vives (14th on Table A1) and Congressman
51:2002:150102:17:17:82:543:594:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Alfonso Campo, one of the signatories at Sante F-e de Ralito, won in each municipality. The map
51:2003:150197:17:17:82:543:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:shows the dramatic increase in electoral concentration in 2002. In particular, in the dark red areas
51:2004:150297:17:17:82:543:560:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:speci\fc politicians were winning essentially 100% of the votes cast in a municipality. One sees
51:2005:150393:17:17:82:543:543:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:that Vives and Campo won very large proportions of votes in the southernmost municipalities
51:2006:150484:17:17:82:543:526:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:such as San Sebasti-an and Guamal. In the dark red municipalities to the north Senators Salom-on
51:2007:150580:17:17:82:543:509:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Saade and Dieb Maloof won nearly all of the votes (2nd and 5th in Table 1, 3rd and 4th in Table
51:2008:150675:17:17:82:543:492:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A1).  Vives, Maloof and Saade all represented third parties and Vives and Maloof have been
51:2009:150765:17:17:82:543:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:tried and found guilty of links with paramilitaries, while Saade is currently under investigation.
51:2010:150863:17:17:82:543:458:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:Concentration falls in 2006 however and Vives wins large proportions of his vote in municipalities
51:2011:150961:17:17:82:543:441:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:to the north, such as El Pinon and San Antonio, where in 2002 he had won no votes. Campo's
51:2012:151051:17:17:82:543:424:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:vote also becomes more evenly distributed over the Department, though he was not re-elected in
51:2013:151145:17:17:82:543:407:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:2006. The pattern is similar for the other Senators and despite of this fall, Maloof and Vives were
51:2014:151244:17:17:82:543:390:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:both re-elected, with almost the same number of votes as in 2006. For example Vives got 53,759
51:2015:151338:17:17:82:289:373:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:in Magdalena in 2002 and 54,609 in 2006.46
51:2016:151380:17:17:99:543:356:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:In 2006 Jos-e Joaqu--n Vives, a Congressman for Magdalena prior to 2002 whose vote share
51:2017:151468:17:29:82:260:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:collapsed in the 2002 elections, noted
51:2018:151506:29:17:126:516:310:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:\Certain Congressmembers have credentials that are built upon the blood of inno-
51:2019:151586:17:17:110:516:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:cent citizens ... In Magdalena circumstances still do not exist for the next election to
51:2020:151674:17:17:110:516:276:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:be free. It must also be said clearly and directly that democracy has been kidnapped
51:2021:151758:17:17:110:516:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:in the department and remains kidnapped through a relationship created between
51:2022:151836:17:29:110:364:242:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f5:certain political groups and the self-defense forces."47

51:2026:152174:16:15:91:543:163:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:46Prior to the 2006 congressional elections two pro-Uribe parties dropped \fve candidates from their lists who
51:2027:152284:15:11:82:543:148:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:were accused of having direct links with paramilitaries. The U party dropped Habib Merheg, Dieb Maloof and Luis
51:2028:152395:11:11:82:543:137:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Eduardo Vives and Cambio Radical dropped Jorge Caballero and Jorge Castro. Expelled candidates re-appeared
51:2029:152501:11:11:82:543:126:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:on the lists of smaller pro-Uribe parties and Merheg and Maloof won seats in Congress with the Colombia Viva
51:2030:152609:11:7:82:106:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Party.
